Introducing Jadal al-Usuliyyin
Title page introducing the book's subject, author, and publisher.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the subject and scope of the book Jadal al-Usuliyyin from its title page.

Core Idea
This book applies jadal to usul al-fiqh, bridging theory and practice.

The title page of a book often reveals its core subject and approach. In this case, the title 'Jadal al-Usuliyyin' indicates a focus on dialectic as practiced by scholars of usul al-fiqh. The subtitle 'Between Theory and Practice' promises a balanced treatment, combining abstract principles with real-world application. This lesson unpacks what the title page tells us about the work's content and significance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main title and subtitle
The main title is 'Al-Jadal' (Dialectic) and the subtitle specifies 'Al-Usuliyyin' (The Usulis). Together they define the subject: dialectic as applied by scholars of usul al-fiqh.
Usul al-fiqh is the science of legal methodology.
2
Note the series and author
The book is part of the 'Al-Rushd Series of University Theses', indicating it is an academic work. The author is a professor at the University of Batna, Algeria, lending scholarly credibility.
3
Understand the significance of 'Between Theory and Practice'
This subtitle indicates that the book does not only discuss theoretical principles of jadal but also illustrates how they are applied in actual juristic debates. This practical focus is crucial for students who want to use jadal in real argumentation.
4
Reflect on the book's promise
From this page, a reader expects a work that explains the rules of usuli dialectic and demonstrates their use. The book likely covers both the theoretical foundations (e.g., definitions and conditions of valid jadal) and case studies from usul al-fiqh literature.

Commentary
This passage is a title page. It presents the book's series, title, subtitle, author, and publisher. The book is part of the 'Al-Rushd Series of University Theses', numbered 109. The main title is 'Al-Jadal' (Dialectic) and the subtitle specifies 'Al-Usuliyyin' (The Usulis, i.e., scholars of usul al-fiqh). The subtitle further explains that the work is 'Between Theory and Practice'. The author is 'Dar Kanour Mas'ud bin Musa Faluti' (likely a misreading of 'Doctor' for 'Dar'); he holds a professorship at the University of Batna in Algeria. The publisher is 'Makanah al-Rushd' (probably a branch of Dar al-Rushd). This front matter establishes the identity and scope of the work, which will address the dialectical method (jadal) as applied by usul scholars, balancing theoretical principles with practical application.

Interpreting the Book Title: Jadal Between Theory and Practice
Title or heading announcing the book's subject matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to interpret the scope of a scholarly work from its title and connect it to the discipline of jadal in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
This title announces a work that bridges theory and practice of dialectical argumentation among usul scholars.

A book's title often encapsulates its entire aim. This title introduces the dynamic activity (al-hirak) among scholars of usul al-fiqh, placing it between theoretical principles (al-nazariyya) and practical application (al-tatbiq). Understanding this helps you grasp that the work is not merely abstract logic but a study of how jadal functions in real juristic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify key terms in the title
Locate the main components: al-hirak (movement/activity), al-usuliyyun (scholars of usul al-fiqh), al-nazariyya (theory), and al-tatbiq (practice). Each term points to a distinct aspect of the book's focus.
2
Analyze the relationship between theory and practice
The phrase 'between theory and practice' suggests the book intends to examine how theoretical principles of jadal are implemented in actual debates and rulings. It is not a purely abstract treatise.
3
Connect to the broader discipline of jadal
Recognize that 'al-usuliyyun' places the work firmly within usul al-fiqh, where jadal (dialectical argumentation) is used to resolve disputes over legal methodology. The title hints at the practical dimensions of jadal in juristic reasoning.
This title sets the stage for a work that bridges two levels: the normative rules of debate and their real-world application.

This indicates that the work aims to bridge theoretical principles of jadal with practical application in usul al-fiqh.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Importance of Jadal in Islamic Sciences
Author introduces the topic of jadal and its significance in Islamic scholarly tradition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role and purpose of jadal in Islamic sciences as presented by the author, including its Qur'anic foundation and practical applications.

Core Idea
Jadal is not mere argumentation; it is a disciplined method to reach truth through respectful evidence-based debate.

This lesson introduces you to the concept of jadal (dialectical argumentation) as a foundational tool in Islamic scholarly tradition. The passage presents jadal as a methodology endorsed by the Qur'an and refined by Muslim scholars across centuries, used not only to defend the faith but to resolve scholarly disputes in a respectful manner. Understanding this introduction will help you appreciate how jadal functions as a serious intellectual discipline, not just rhetoric.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's central claim about jadal
Read the opening lines after the basmalah. The author states that jadal is 'one of the most important topics' and 'most worthy of study'. Why? Because it is linked to the Islamic creed from the very beginning.
Look for the phrase 'ارتبط بالعقيدة الإسلامية من أول يوم'
2
Extract the two Qur'anic purposes of jadal
The author says the Qur'an used jadal for two purposes: (1) to silence opponents who reject the creed, and (2) to convince those open to accepting it. Write these down.
The Arabic uses 'إفحام الخصوم' and 'إقناع' those ready to accept.
3
Trace the historical breadth of jadal
The author notes that jadal was not only against non-Muslims but also among Muslims themselves, in all sciences: creed, fiqh, usul, tafsir, hadith. Find where he lists these sciences.
Look for 'العقيدة وفروع الفقه وأصوله ومسائل التفسير والحديث'.
4
Identify the ultimate goal of jadal
The author states the basic benefit: 'ترجيح الصواب وطرح الخطأ' (preferring correctness and discarding error). This is the goal of jadal: truth-seeking, not victory.
Contrast this with common misconception that jadal is simply winning an argument.
5
Understand the author's motivation for the book
The author laments that jadal has been neglected, especially in usul al-fiqh, and that classical works were practical without enough theoretical analysis. This motivates his research.
He mentions specific classical jadal works but notes their lack of theory.

المقدمة

أهمية الموضوع :
الدين
الحمد لله رب العالمين والصلاة والسلام على أشرف المرسلين سيدنا ونبينا محمد وعلى آله وصحبه أجمعين والتابعين ومن تبع هداهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين والعاقبة للمتقين، أما بعد: فيعتبر موضوع الجدل واحدا من أهم الموضوعات وأكثرها أحقية بالدراسة والبحث، فهو موضوع يتناول منهجًا ارتبط بالعقيدة الإسلامية من أول يوم أرسل ببيانها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، إذ اتخذ منه القرآن الكريم وسيلة إلى إفحام الخصوم الرافضين للعقيدة الإسلامية من جهة ووسيلة إلى إقناع أولئك الذين يتوفر لديهم الاستعداد لتقبل هذه العقيدة والحرص على فهم عناصرها من جهة ثانية. وقد استفاد العلماء المسلمون من توجيهات القرآن الكريم وأساليبه الحكيمة في هذا المجال، فاتخذوا من الجدل وسيلة إلى إقناع مخالفيهم في الرأي حتى تحول لديهم إلى صناعة يلجئون إليها إذا ما أرادوا تدارس المسائل وتقليب وجهات النظر وتبادل الرأي فيها حتى يتم الاستقرار على رأي أقرب إلى الصواب في شأنها.
،
فلم يكن الجدل وسيلة إلى إفحام وإقناع مخالفي العقيدة الإسلامية فحسب، بل كان وسيلة كذلك إلى مناقشة وإقناع المسلمين فيما بينهم، وخاصة في الشئون والآراء العلمية المتعلقة بالعقيدة وفروع الفقه وأصوله ومسائل التفسير والحديث، وغيرها من القضايا التي تشغل الفكر الإسلامي. وذلك ما يظهر من خلال الرجوع إلى مؤلفات العلماء المسلمين في سائر علوم الشريعة الإسلامية المتنوعة عبر التاريخ الإسلامي الطويل، حيث نجدها حافلة بالمسائل الخلافية التي يسوقونها في طابع جدلي بحت يعتمد على إيراد الرأي والرأي المخالف وعرض أدلة كل رأي ومناقشتها مناقشة هادئة هادفة . وليست الكتب وحدها الميدان الذي عرف الجدل، فإن تاريخ العلوم في ظل الإسلام يشهد بأن دور العلم وحلقات المساجد ومجالس الحكام كانت قد شهدت الآلاف من المناظرات بين العلماء المسلمين فيما بينهم، أو بينهم وبين غيرهم من علماء الأديان الأخرى، حول مسائل علمية متنوعة بين عقدية وفقهية وأصولية
6
ولغوية وغيرها، وتميزت بتبادل الآراء والحجج ومناقشة المذاهب والأدلة، في أدب جم واحترام متبادل في الغالب، بغية الوصول إلى تحقيق الحق وهو ترجيح الصواب وطرح الخطأ.
وهذا الترجيح بين الآراء والأدلة هو الفائدة الأساس التي يحققها الجدل، حيث يفضي إلى اختيار الرأي الصائب الأقرب إلى الحق وفق ما تقتضيه الأدلة القائمة، وطرح الآراء الأخرى التي لا تسندها أدلة ولا تجد ركائز تقوم عليها، وهو ما يؤدي إلى الاقتراب بالمعلومات والآراء العلمية من الحق والابتعاد بها قدر الإمكان عن الخطأ الذي ربما كان سببا إلى الضلال.
وإذا كان الجدل في العلوم الإسلامية بهذه المكانة والأهمية فقد كان جديرا بأن يكون موضع بحث ودراسة من طرف الباحثين والدارسين المسلمين الذين أخذوا على عاتقهم مهمة استجلاء جوانب الشموخ والعظمة في التراث الإسلامي وعلومه، وإبراز مظاهر التفرد والإبداع في هذا التراث حتى تترسمها الأجيال وتتقفى آثار الأسلاف فيها، لكن المؤسف أن هذا الموضوع لم يلق العناية اللازمة إلا في القليل النادر، وإذا كان قد لفت نوعا من الانتباه في دراسات علم الكلام، فإنه في علم أصول الفقه لم يحظ من اهتمام الدارسين إلا بالتفاتات نادرة. أسباب اختيار البحث : وقد دعاني إلى اختيار هذا الموضوع لتناوله في رسالة جامعية لنيل شهادة دكتوراه الدولة في العلوم الإسلامية :

Dialectics
Introduction
5
Importance of the Topic:
Religion
Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and peace and blessings be upon the most honorable of messengers, our master and prophet Muhammad, and upon his family and all his companions, and the followers, and those who follow their guidance with excellence until the Day of Judgment, and the end is for the righteous. As to proceed: The topic of jadal is considered one of the most important topics and the most worthy of study and research. It is a topic that deals with a methodology linked to the Islamic creed from the first day the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was sent to explain it. The Qur'an used it as a means to silence opponents who reject the Islamic creed on one hand, and as a means to convince those who have the readiness to accept this creed and are keen to understand its elements on the other hand. Muslim scholars benefited from the guidance of the Qur'an and its wise methods in this field. They adopted jadal as a means to convince their opponents in opinion, so much so that it became a craft they resort to whenever they wish to study issues, exchange viewpoints, and discuss opinions until they settle on an opinion closer to correctness regarding the matter.

Thus, jadal was not only a means to silence and convince opponents of the Islamic creed, but also a means for Muslims to discuss and convince among themselves, especially in scholarly matters and opinions related to creed, branches of jurisprudence, its principles, issues of exegesis and hadith, and other issues that occupy Islamic thought. This is evident from referring to the works of Muslim scholars in all the diverse Islamic sciences throughout the long Islamic history. We find them full of controversial issues presented in a purely dialectical character, based on presenting the opinion and the opposing opinion, presenting the evidence for each opinion, and discussing them calmly and purposefully. Books are not the only field where jadal was known, for the history of sciences under Islam testifies that study circles, mosque gatherings, and rulers' councils witnessed thousands of debates among Muslim scholars themselves, or between them and scholars of other religions, on various scholarly issues, doctrinal, jurisprudential, foundational, and linguistic among others. These debates were characterized by an exchange of opinions and arguments, and discussion of schools and evidence, with great etiquette and mutual respect for the most part, aiming to achieve truth, which is preferring correctness and discarding error.

This preference between opinions and evidence is the basic benefit achieved by jadal. It leads to choosing the correct opinion closest to the truth according to the available evidence, and discarding other opinions that are not supported by evidence and lack foundations. This brings scholarly information and opinions closer to the truth and distances them as much as possible from error, which might be a cause of misguidance.

Since jadal in the Islamic sciences holds this status and importance, it deserved to be a subject of research and study by Muslim researchers and scholars who have taken upon themselves the task of elucidating the aspects of sublimity and greatness in the Islamic heritage and its sciences, and highlighting the manifestations of uniqueness and creativity in this heritage so that generations may follow and emulate the footsteps of their predecessors. However, unfortunately, this topic has not received the necessary attention except rarely. If it has attracted some attention in studies of kalam, then in usul al-fiqh it has not received from the attention of researchers except rare glances.

Reasons for Choosing the Research:
What urged me to choose this topic for a university thesis for a Doctorat d'État in Islamic sciences:
A - What I mentioned about the lack of attention to this topic... It is true that our early scholars dealt with the topic of jadal and wrote famous books on it, including 'Al-Mu'wanah fi al-Jadal' by Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, 'Al-Minhaj fi Tartib al-Hijaj' by Abu al-Walid al-Baji, 'Al-Kafiyah fi al-Jadal' by Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, 'Al-Jadal 'ala Tariqah al-Fuqaha'' by Ibn 'Aqil al-Hanbali, and ' 'Ilm al-Jadhl fi 'Ilm al-Jadal' by Najm al-Din al-Tufi. However, the prevailing character of these books is the applied presentation, without much attention to analysis and theorization except a little. Moreover, these books overlap in the topics of Islamic sciences significantly, especially the topics of kalam, fiqh, and usul al-fiqh. This needs...
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the introduction to a book on jadal (dialectics) by a modern scholar, outlining the importance of the topic and the motivation for the research. The author begins with the basmalah and praise, then states that jadal is one of the most worthy subjects for study because it is a methodology intimately linked to the Islamic creed from the very beginning of revelation. The Quran itself employed jadal both to silence opponents and to convince those open to the faith. Muslim scholars later adopted this method, turning it into a craft for debating and reaching sound opinions. The author then expands on the scope of jadal: it was not limited to confronting non-Muslims but was used among Muslims themselves in all scholarly fields—creed, fiqh, usul, tafsir, hadith, etc. This is evidenced by the many works containing dialectical discussions. Furthermore, jadal was practiced in study circles, mosques, and courts, with thousands of debates characterized by respectful exchange aimed at truth. The core benefit of jadal, the author explains, is the weighing of opinions and evidence to choose the truth and discard error. Given its importance, the author regrets that jadal has not received sufficient scholarly attention, especially in usul al-fiqh. Finally, the author states the reasons for choosing this topic: the lack of care, noting that while classical scholars wrote applied works on jadal, they lacked theoretical analysis, and these works overlap with other sciences, thus necessitating a dedicated study.

Key Takeaway

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
The Nature and Purpose of Jadal in Islamic Sciences
Author describes the nature and purpose of jadal and its neglect in scholarship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define jadal and explain its primary benefit of tarjih al-sawab (preferring correctness) using the author's description.

Core Idea
Jadal is not mere argument but a disciplined pursuit of truth through evidence and etiquette.

Jadal (dialectical debate) is often misunderstood as adversarial wrangling. In this passage, the author clarifies that jadal in the Islamic tradition is a structured exchange aimed at reaching truth by weighing evidences. He also bemoans its neglect, especially in usul al-fiqh. This lesson unpacks the definition and purpose of jadal as presented by the author.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of jadal
Find the opening sentence where the author describes jadal as an exchange of opinions and arguments. Note the emphasis on mutual respect and etiquette.
The Arabic term 'الجدل' is defined not just linguistically but as a disciplined practice.
2
Extract the purpose of jadal
Identify the phrase 'ترجيح الصواب وطرح الخطأ' (preferring correctness and discarding error). This is the ultimate goal of jadal.
The author calls this the 'fundamental benefit' (الفائدة الأساس).
3
Analyze the mechanism
Notice that jadal works by comparing evidences (أدلة) and selecting the opinion closest to the truth based on evidence strength. Unsupported views are discarded.
This is a rational process, not a display of rhetoric.
4
Identify the author's lament
In the latter part, the author states that jadal has been neglected, especially in usul al-fiqh. Despite its importance, it received only rare attention.
Contrast the respectful, evidence-based ideal with the lack of scholarly focus.

الجدل ولغوية وغيرها، وتميزت بتبادل الآراء والحجج ومناقشة المذاهب والأدلة، في أدب جم واحترام متبادل في الغالب، بغية الوصول إلى تحقيق الحق وهو ترجيح الصواب وطرح الخطأ. وهذا الترجيح بين الآراء والأدلة هو الفائدة الأساس التي يحققها الجدل، حيث يفضي إلى اختيار الرأي الصائب الأقرب إلى الحق وفق ما تقتضيه الأدلة القائمة، وطرح الآراء الأخرى التي لا تسندها أدلة ولا تجد ركائز تقوم عليها، وهو ما يؤدي إلى الاقتراب بالمعلومات والآراء العلمية من الحق والابتعاد بها قدر الإمكان عن الخطأ الذي ربما كان سببا إلى الضلال. وإذا كان الجدل في العلوم الإسلامية بهذه المكانة والأهمية فقد كان جديرا بأن يكون موضع بحث ودراسة من طرف الباحثين والدارسين المسلمين الذين أخذوا على عاتقهم مهمة استجلاء جوانب الشموخ والعظمة في التراث الإسلامي وعلومه، وإبراز مظاهر التفرد والإبداع في هذا التراث حتى تترسمها الأجيال وتتقفى آثار الأسلاف فيها، لكن المؤسف أن هذا الموضوع لم يلق العناية اللازمة إلا في القليل النادر، وإذا كان قد لفت نوعا من الانتباه في دراسات علم الكلام، فإنه في علم أصول الفقه لم يحظ من اهتمام الدارسين إلا بالتفاتات نادرة.
Jadal, linguistic and other, is distinguished by the exchange of opinions and arguments and the discussion of doctrines and evidences, with refined decorum and mutual respect mostly, aiming to reach the realization of truth, which is preferring correctness and discarding error. This preference among opinions and evidences is the fundamental benefit that jadal achieves, as it leads to choosing the correct opinion closest to the truth according to what the existing evidences require, and discarding other opinions that are not supported by evidence and do not find foundations to stand on, and this leads to bringing information and scientific opinions closer to the truth and distancing them as much as possible from error which might be a cause of misguidance. Since jadal in the Islamic sciences holds this status and importance, it deserved to be a subject of research and study by Muslim researchers and scholars who have taken upon themselves the task of clarifying aspects of glory and greatness in the Islamic heritage and its sciences, and highlighting manifestations of uniqueness and creativity in this heritage so that generations may follow in its footsteps and emulate the traces of their predecessors. But unfortunately, this topic has not received the necessary attention except rarely, and if it has attracted some attention in the studies of kalam, then in the science of usul al-fiqh it has not received from the interest of scholars except rare glances.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is an introduction that defines the concept of jadal (dialectical debate) and its purpose in Islamic sciences. The author begins by stating that jadal is characterized by the exchange of opinions and arguments, with mutual respect and etiquette, aiming to reach truth by preferring correct opinions and discarding error. This preference between opinions and evidences is the primary benefit of jadal. The author emphasizes that jadal leads to selecting the correct view supported by evidence and discarding unsupported views, thus bringing knowledge closer to truth and away from error. The author then highlights the high status of jadal in Islamic sciences and argues that it deserves scholarly attention. However, he laments that the topic has been neglected, receiving only rare attention in kalam studies and even less in usul al-fiqh. This sets the stage for the author's own research.

Jadal is an evidence-based, respectful dialectical method aimed at tarjih al-sawab (preferring correctness) and avoiding error.

?

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
Identifying Research Gaps in Jadal Literature
Author presents reasons for his research on jadal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a research gap in classical Islamic scholarship by analyzing the applied vs theoretical nature of works.

Core Idea
Classical jadal literature is rich in application but poor in theoretical analysis.

When studying classical Islamic disciplines, it is easy to assume that earlier scholars covered everything. However, careful reading often reveals gaps. In this passage, the author argues that classical jadal works are overwhelmingly applied (tatbiqi) with little theorization. This observation forms the foundation for his entire doctoral research. Understanding how to spot such a gap is crucial for any researcher in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
List the classical jadal works mentioned
Identify the books and authors listed by the author: al-Mu'wana fi al-Jadal by al-Shirazi, al-Minhaj by al-Baji, al-Kafiya by al-Juwayni, al-Jadal 'ala Tariqat al-Fuqaha' by Ibn 'Aqil, and 'Ilm al-Jadhal by al-Tufi. Notice they span different centuries and madhabs.
This list is not exhaustive but representative of the genre.
2
Identify what the author says is missing
The author states that the dominant character is 'applied presentation' (al-'ard al-tatbiqi) without 'analysis and theorization' (al-tahlil wa al-tanzir). This is the gap: lack of theoretical framework.
Distinguish between 'applied' (how to do jadal) and 'theoretical' (what is jadal, its principles, its epistemological status).
3
Understand why this gap matters for usul al-fiqh
The author notes that these jadal works interweave topics from kalam, fiqh, and usul al-fiqh. A theoretical separation is needed to extract the specifically usuli contributions, which is the author's goal.
The gap is not just absence of theory, but also confusion of disciplinary boundaries.
4
Recognize how the author's own experience led to the gap
The author discovered the gap during his master's thesis on the School of Theologians, where he observed applied jadal but no theory. This personal observation is a typical starting point for research.
A research gap often emerges from direct engagement with primary sources.

Reasons for choosing the research: I was led to choose this topic to address it in a university thesis for obtaining a state doctorate in Islamic sciences: A - What I mentioned about the lack of attention to this topic. It is true that our ancient scholars addressed the topic of jadal and prepared well-known books on it, including al-Mu'wana fi al-Jadal by Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, and al-Minhaj fi Tartib al-Hijaj by Abu al-Walid al-Baji, and al-Kafiya fi al-Jadal by Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, and al-Jadal 'ala Tariqat al-Fuqaha' by Ibn 'Aqil al-Hanbali, and 'Ilm al-Jadhal fi 'Ilm al-Jadal by Najm al-Din al-Tufi. However, the dominant character of these books is the applied presentation, without attention to analysis and theorization except a little. Moreover, these books interweave the subjects of Islamic sciences clearly, especially the subjects of kalam, fiqh, and usul al-fiqh. This requires a separating effort to distinguish between these subjects and extract those related to usul al-fiqh separately. As for contemporary scholars, I do not know anyone who drew attention to studying the idea of jadal among the usuliyyin except the Tunisian researcher Dr. 'Abd al-Majid Turki, who edited the books Ihkam al-Fusul fi Ahkam al-Usul and al-Minhaj fi Tartib al-Hijaj by al-Baji, and the books Sharh al-Luma' fi Usul al-Fiqh and al-Mu'wana fi al-Jadal by al-Shirazi, and authored a book titled Munazarat fi Usul al-Shari'a al-Islamiyya bayna Ibn Hazm wa al-Baji. He alerted in all these works to the importance of this topic, but what he wrote about it does not exceed faint indications without penetrating its depth through study and analysis. - Various forms (The other reason that led me to choose this topic is that the abundant dialectical richness prevalent in books of usul al-fiqh caught my attention when I was preparing my master's thesis on the topic 'The School of Theologians and its Method in Studying Usul al-Fiqh Rules', where I noticed the usuliyyin's use of various methods of jadal and their treatment of objecting to the opinions and evidences of opponents. However, that use was applied, not theoretical, meaning they expanded in treating jadal as application, but they did not address its theoretical aspects except rarely. I had, for that reason, included in that thesis a brief section on jadal among the usuliyyin, but it was just a section not exceeding a few pages that did not suffice for this broad and extensive topic. Therefore, I decided to continue researching the topic in a thesis for obtaining a state doctorate, which I have done in the thesis before the reader, and praise be to God. Research problematic and its objectives: From the above, we can precisely determine the problematic that this research addresses, which is: What is the reality of jadal among the usuliyyin? Does it have roots in Islamic thought? What are its theoretical elements, intellectual foundations, and practical steps? Then, how were those theoretical foundations and steps applied when disagreeing in

Commentary
This passage is the author's explanation of his motivation for the research and the questions he seeks to answer. It begins with the first reason: the lack of scholarly attention. The author acknowledges that classical scholars wrote works on jadal, listing several titles such as al-Mu'wana fi al-Jadal by al-Shirazi, al-Minhaj by al-Baji, al-Kafiya by al-Juwayni, and others. However, he notes that these works are primarily applied (tatbiqi) and lack theoretical analysis. Furthermore, the topics are interwoven with other Islamic sciences, so a separating effort is needed to extract the usul al-fiqh related aspects. Then the author mentions contemporary contributions, specifically the Tunisian researcher Dr. 'Abd al-Majid Turki, who edited several key texts but only provided faint indications on the subject. The second reason is the author's personal observation from his master's thesis: he saw that usuliyyin used jadal extensively in practice but did not develop a theoretical framework. This prompted him to write a brief section, which was insufficient, leading to the current doctoral work. Finally, the author formulates the research problematic with several questions: the reality of jadal among usuliyyin, its Islamic roots, its theoretical elements, foundations, practical steps, and how they were applied in cases of disagreement. The text ends abruptly but clearly states the core questions.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Formulating Research Problematic in Islamic Studies
Author formulates the research problematic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to formulate a research problematic consisting of structured questions based on a preliminary observation.

Core Idea
A good research problematic asks 'what', 'why', and 'how' about the subject.

After identifying a research gap, the next step is to articulate clear questions that guide the investigation. In this passage, the author moves from his observation (lack of theoretical jadal) to a set of precise questions about the reality, roots, elements, and application of jadal among usuliyyin. Learning to formulate such a problematic is a key skill for any Islamic studies researcher.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's initial observation
The author observed that jadal is used extensively in usul al-fiqh books but in an applied manner. This observation is the foundation for the problematic.
A problematic always stems from an observation that raises questions.
2
Note the questions the author poses
The author asks: 'What is the reality of jadal among usuliyyin? Does it have roots in Islamic thought? What are its theoretical elements, intellectual foundations, and practical steps? Then, how were these applied when disagreeing?' These are four question types: definition, origin, components, and application.
Notice the progression: from essence to genealogy to structure to function.
3
See how these questions follow from the gap
The gap (applied without theory) leads directly to the first question about 'reality' – which would clarify whether there is an implicit theoretical framework. The other questions probe the dimensions needed to construct a theory.
The gap determines the scope of the problematic.

However, he notes that these works are primarily applied (tatbiqi) and lack theoretical analysis. Then the author mentions contemporary contributions, specifically the Tunisian researcher Dr. 'Abd al-Majid Turki, who edited several key texts but only provided faint indications on the subject. The second reason is the author's personal observation from his master's thesis: he saw that usuliyyin used jadal extensively in practice but did not develop a theoretical framework. This prompted him to write a brief section, which was insufficient, leading to the current doctoral work. Finally, the author formulates the research problematic with several questions: the reality of jadal among usuliyyin, its Islamic roots, its theoretical elements, foundations, practical steps, and how they were applied in cases of disagreement. The text ends abruptly but clearly states the core questions.

Distinguishing Applied from Theoretical Jadal
Author explains the imbalance between applied and theoretical jadal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between applied (tatbiqi) and theoretical (nazari) jadal as used by Islamic legal theorists, and identify why this distinction marks a scholarly gap.

Core Idea
Jadal was practiced extensively but theorized scarcely—this gap drives the author's entire research.

The author opens by noting a curious imbalance in the study of jadal. While usuliyyin used dialectical methods routinely in their works, almost no one had systematically analyzed the theory behind those methods. Understanding this imbalance is key to appreciating why the author's book exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two uses of jadal mentioned
Find the terms 'tatbiqi' and 'nazari' in the Arabic passage and note their contrast.
2
Observe the author's evidence for the applied use
The author says usuliyyin expanded in using jadal to object to opponents.
3
Locate the gap he identifies
He says they rarely addressed theoretical aspects. This is the gap.
4
Connect this gap to his research trajectory
The author first covered it briefly in his Master's, then dedicated his doctorate to it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما عند المعاصرين فلا أعرف من لفت الانتباه إلى دراسة فكرة الجدل عند الأصوليين سوى الباحث التونسي الدكتور عبد المجيد تركي، الذي حقق كتابي إحكام الفصول في أحكام الأصول) و(المنهاج في ترتيب الحجاج للباجي، وكتابي (شرح اللمع في أصول الفقه) و(المعونة في الجدل) للشيرازي، وألف كتابا بعنوان (مناظرات في أصول الشريعة الإسلامية بين ابن حزم والباجي)، وقد نبه في هذه الأعمال كلها إلى أهمية هذا الموضوع لكن ما كتبه فيه لا يتعدى مجرد إشارات خافتة دون النفاذ إلى عمقه بالدرس والتحليل . - لمختلف صور ( أما السبب الآخر الذي دعاني إلى اختيار هذا الموضوع، فهو أن الثراء الجدلي الغالب على كتب أصول الفقه قد لفت انتباهي عندما كنت أعد رسالتي لنيل شهادة الماجستير في موضوع (مدرسة المتكلمين ومنهجها في دراسة القواعد الأصولية)، حيث لاحظت استخدام الأصوليين مختلف أساليب الجدل وتناولهم الاعتراض على آراء المخالفين وأدلتهم، إلا أن استخدامهم ذاك كان استخدامًا تطبيقيًا لا نظريًا، بمعنى أنهم توسعوا في تناول الجدل كتطبيق، لكنهم لم يتناولوا جوانبه النظرية إلا القليل النادر . وقد كنت عقدت لأجل ذلك في رسالتي تلك مبحثا موجزا عن الجدل عند الأصوليين، لكنه كان مجرد مبحث لا يتعدى صفحات قليلة لا تفي بهذا الموضوع الواسع الأطراف الطويل الذيول، ولذلك قررت أن أستمر في البحث في الموضوع في رسالة أعدها لنيل شهادة دكتوراه الدولة، وهو ما قمت به في الرسالة التي بين يدي القارئ، والحمد لله .
As for contemporary researchers, I know of no one who has drawn attention to the study of the concept of jadal among the usuliyyin except the Tunisian researcher Dr. Abdul Majid Turki, who edited the books 'Ihkam al-Fusul fi Ahkam al-Usul' and 'al-Minhaj fi Tartib al-Hijaj' by al-Baji, and the two books 'Sharh al-Luma' fi Usul al-Fiqh' and 'al-Ma'unah fi al-Jadal' by al-Shirazi, and authored a book titled 'Munazarat fi Usul al-Shari'ah al-Islamiyyah bayn Ibn Hazm wa al-Baji'. In all these works he has drawn attention to the importance of this subject, but his writings on it do not go beyond faint indications without penetrating its depth through study and analysis. The other reason that led me to choose this subject is that the prevalent dialectical richness in the books of usul al-fiqh caught my attention when I was preparing my thesis for the Master's degree on the topic 'The School of the Theologians and its Methodology in Studying Usul al-Fiqh Rules', where I observed the usuliyyin's use of various methods of jadal and their handling of objections to the opinions and evidences of opponents, except that their use was applied, not theoretical – meaning they expanded in treating jadal as an application, but they scarcely addressed its theoretical aspects except rarely. For that reason, I included in that thesis a brief section on jadal among the usuliyyin, but it was merely a section not exceeding a few pages, insufficient for this vast topic with far-reaching implications. Therefore I decided to continue researching the subject in a thesis for the Doctorat d'État degree, which is what I have done in the present work, and praise be to God.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage presents the author's academic motivation for studying jadal among Islamic legal theorists (usuliyyin). The author first acknowledges the work of Dr. Abdul Majid Turki, who drew attention to the subject through his editions and his book on debates between Ibn Hazm and al-Baji, but notes that Turki's contributions are only faint indications without deep analysis. The author then explains his personal impetus: during his Master's thesis, he observed that usuliyyin applied jadal extensively in their works—using dialectical methods to object to opponents—but did not develop a systematic theoretical framework for it. They treated jadal purely as a practical tool. This gap motivated the author to first write a brief section in his Master's thesis, and then to dedicate his doctoral dissertation to a thorough investigation of jadal, the result of which is the present book.

Understanding the Research Problem and Objectives
Author defines the central research problem and lists four specific research objectives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main research problem and the four sub-objectives of a study on jadal in usul al-fiqh, and explain how they structure the research.

Core Idea
A clear research problem and sub-objectives give direction to scholarly inquiry.

In academic research, defining the problem and objectives is crucial. This passage sets out the central questions the author will address about jadal (dialectical method) among usuliyyin (Islamic legal theorists). The problem is broken into two key questions: Is there a theory of jadal? Are there applications? Four sub-objectives then guide the investigation. By parsing this structure, you learn how to frame research in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central research problem
Find the main question(s) the author poses about jadal in usul al-fiqh. The passage begins with 'What is the reality of jadal among the usuliyyin?' and ends with two overarching questions: whether there is a theory and whether there are applications.
The problem is not a single question but a cluster of interconnected inquiries.
2
Distinguish the two overarching questions
The author condenses the problem into two: (1) Is there a theory of jadal? and (2) Are there applications of that theory? These guide the entire study.
These questions are foundational; the sub-objectives are designed to answer them.
3
Locate the four sub-objectives
The passage lists four sub-objectives (a–d). Read each carefully: (a) gather and systematize elements, (b) explain roots and motives, (c) highlight differentiation across studies, (d) show role in developing usul al-fiqh.
Each sub-objective addresses a distinct aspect of the main problem.
4
Understand the relationship
The sub-objectives collectively answer the two main questions. For example, objective (a) builds the theory, while (d) shows applications. Objectives (b) and (c) provide historical context.
This structure is typical in Islamic scholarship: first clarify the problem, then break it into manageable parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إشكالية البحث وأهدافه : مما سبق يمكن أن نحدد الإشكالية التي يتناولها هذا البحث بدقة، وهي: ما حقيقة الجدل عند الأصوليين؟ وهل له جذور في الفكر الإسلامي؟ وما هي عناصره النظرية وأسسه الفكرية التي يقوم عليها وخطواته العملية التي يسير وفقها ..؟ ثم كيف تم تطبيق تلك الأسس والخطوات النظرية عند الاختلاف في المسائل العملية؟ وما هي هذه المسائل أساسا ؟ وباختصار يمكن أن نطرح التساؤل بالصيغة الآتية: هل للجدل نظرية عند الأصوليين، وما هي هذه النظرية؟ وهل له تطبيقات، وما هي هذه التطبيقات؟ التساؤل الرئيس الذي حاولت الوصول إليه من خلال تحقيق جملة من هذا هو الأهداف الجزئية، هي: أ - تجميع عناصر موضوع الجدل النظرية والتطبيقية عند الأصوليين، وسبكها في بناء منهجي يجعل معالم الموضوع واضحة وإسهامات الأصوليين فيه بارزة بكل جلاء ووضوح. ب – بيان جذور الجدل في الفكر الأصولي، والدوافع التي دفعت الأصوليين إلى التفنن في استخدامه وإبداعهم في ابتكار أساليبه ومناهجه. ج - إبراز تمايز الدراسات الأصولية فيما بينها في شأن استخدام الجدل وقوة ظهوره في هذه الدراسات عبر مراحل ظهورها. د – إبراز الدور الذي لعبه المنهج الجدلي في تطوير علم أصول الفقه وإثراء موضوعاته بمباحث جديدة كانت تظهر مع تقدم هذا العلم وتطوره.
The Research Problem and Its Objectives: From the above, we can precisely define the problem addressed by this research, which is: What is the reality of jadal among the usuliyyin? Does it have roots in Islamic thought? What are its theoretical elements and intellectual foundations upon which it is based, and its practical steps according to which it proceeds? Then how were those theoretical foundations and steps applied when differing over practical issues? And what are these issues fundamentally? In short, we can pose the question in the following form: Is there a theory of jadal among the usuliyyin, and what is this theory? Are there applications of it, and what are these applications? This is the main question that I have attempted to achieve through realizing a number of sub-objectives, which are: a) To gather the theoretical and applied elements of the subject of jadal among the usuliyyin, and to forge them into a systematic structure that makes the features of the subject clear and the contributions of the usuliyyin prominent with full clarity and transparency. b) To elucidate the roots of jadal in usuli thought, and the motives that drove the usuliyyin to excel in its use and their creativity in inventing its methods and approaches. c) To highlight the differentiation among usuli studies regarding the use of jadal and the strength of its appearance in these studies across the stages of their emergence. d) To highlight the role played by the dialectical method (al-manhaj al-jadali) in developing the science of usul al-fiqh and enriching its topics with new discussions that appeared with the progress and development of this science.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage defines the research problem and enumerates four objectives. The author first sharpens the central problem into a series of precise questions: What is the reality of jadal among usuliyyin? Does it have Islamic roots? What are its theoretical elements, intellectual foundations, and practical steps? How were these applied in real legal disputes? He then condenses these into two overarching questions: Is there a theory of jadal? Are there applications? To answer these, he sets four sub-objectives: (a) to gather and systematize the theoretical and applied elements of jadal, (b) to explain its roots and the motives behind the usuliyyin's mastery of it, (c) to show how different usuli works varied in their use of jadal over time, and (d) to demonstrate how the dialectical method contributed to the development of usul al-fiqh itself by generating new topics.

Research Framework for Jadal Usuliyyin
Author outlines research questions, objectives, methodology, and structure for studying jadal usuliyyin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main components of a research framework for studying jadal usuliyyin as presented by the author, including the central question, sub-objectives, methodological foundations, and research plan.

Core Idea
The study of jadal combines historical, inductive, and analytical methods to uncover theory and practice.

This passage is the introduction to a research work on jadal (dialectical reasoning) as practiced by usuliyyun. The author sets the stage by posing a central research question and outlining a multi-method approach. Understanding this framework is crucial for anyone studying how Islamic scholars structured their investigation of jadal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central research question
Find the main question the author poses about jadal among the usuliyyun. The question is whether there is a theory of jadal among them and what its applications are.
2
List the four sub-objectives
The author breaks down the main question into four goals: (A) gather theoretical and practical elements, (B) explain roots and motives, (C) highlight differentiation across studies, (D) show jadal's role in developing usul al-fiqh.
3
Examine the four methodological foundations
The methodology combines history (tracing roots), induction (extracting theory from writings), analysis (identifying common elements), and balance between theory and practice.
Note that induction was used more for theory because the theoretical side was lacking.
4
Understand the research plan structure
The research is divided into a preliminary section on historical roots, then two main sections: theory and application. Each section is further subdivided into chapters, topics, and sub-topics.

تجميع عناصر موضوع الجدل النظرية والتطبيقية عند الأصوليين، وسبكها في بناء منهجي يجعل معالم الموضوع واضحة وإسهامات الأصوليين فيه بارزة بكل جلاء ووضوح. ب – بيان جذور الجدل في الفكر الأصولي، والدوافع التي دفعت الأصوليين إلى التفنن في استخدامه وإبداعهم في ابتكار أساليبه ومناهجه. ج - إبراز تمايز الدراسات الأصولية فيما بينها في شأن استخدام الجدل وقوة ظهوره في هذه الدراسات عبر مراحل ظهورها. د – إبراز الدور الذي لعبه المنهج الجدلي في تطوير علم أصول الفقه وإثراء موضوعاته بمباحث جديدة كانت تظهر مع تقدم هذا العلم وتطوره. منهج البحث : لقد رأيت بالنظر إلى طبيعة الموضوع أن تحقيق هذه الأهداف، يقتضي السير من الأسس المستمدة من أكثر من منهج، وهذه على منهج دقيق يجمع الأسس هي: أ - التأريخ: إذ أن هذا الموضوع له طبيعة تاريخية، فقد اقتضاني تتبع جذور الجدل في الفكر الإسلامي وإسهامات الأصوليين في البحث الجدلي إلى النبش في كتب التاريخ والتراجم والموسوعات الخاصة بالتأريخ للكتب والمؤلفات، في محاولة للوقوف على عناوين الكتب التي تتعلق بموضوع الجدل منسوبة إلى مؤلفيها ، ثم البحث في سير هؤلاء المؤلفين لتحديد الفترات التاريخية التي ينتمون إليها، ثم محاولة الوقوف على طبيعة الإسهام الذي قدمه كل منهم في هذا المجال . ب - الاستقراء : وهذا الأساس إنما استعملته في الجانب النظري أكثر منه في الجانب التطبيقي، وما ذلك إلا لأن هذا الموضوع إنما يعاني من النقص أساسا في جانبه النظري، ولذلك حاولت أن أستخلص الأسس النظرية للمنهج الجدلي عند الأصوليين من واقع مؤلفاتهم في علم أصول الفقه كما طبقته كذلك في الجانب التطبيقي ولكن بصورة أقل، لأن الأصوليين تناولوا هذه التطبيقات في عدد من مؤلفاتهم، ولذلك فإن استقرائي لها كان عبارة عن تجميع وإعادة عرض ما جمعته من مادة. ج - التحليل : وهو النتيجة الطبيعية للاستقراء، فقد أفضى علمية تطبيقية من كتب الأصوليين إلى تحليلها وملاحظة العناصر المشتركة بينها، وعن طريق ذلك توصلت إلى ضبط الكثير من العناوين النظرية التي ينطوي عليها هذا البحث . د - التوازن بين النظرية والتطبيق : وهذا أساس منهجي حَكَمَ بحثي من بدايته إلى نهايته، فقد حاولت - نظرًا لطبيعة الموضوع - أن أحافظ على هذا التوازن، وأعمل على ألا يغلب أحد طرفي الموضوع على الآخر، وأحسب أني نجحت في ذلك بحمد الله عز وجل، لكن لابد من الإشارة إلى أن مادة الموضوع في موقع من مواقع البحث قد تكون قليلة جدًا أحيانًا، ولذلك لا يمكنني أن أحافظ في هذا الموقع على مبدأ التوازن فلا شك أن طبيعة الموضوع وطبيعة كل عنصر من عناصره والمادة العلمية المتصلة به كل ذلك له تأثير في هذا الإطار . خطة البحث : لقد اقتضتني الأهداف التي حاولت الوصول إليها، وطبيعة المنهج الذي سرت عليه أن أقسم الموضوع إلى قسمين رئيسين، أحدهما أخصصه للنظرية، والثاني للتطبيق، ولما كان الموضوع يضرب بجذوره في أعماق التاريخ وأصوله تاريخية أساسا، فقد كان لابد من أن أخصص للجانب التاريخي مجاله اللازم في البحث لكن على سبيل اعتباره مدخلا إلى البحث لا من صلبه . ولذلك جاء هذا البحث مقسما إلى باب تمهيدي وبابين اثنين أساسين، وكل باب من الثلاثة ينقسم إلى فصول وكل فصل إلى مباحث، وكل مبحث إلى مطالب، تبعا لنوعية المادة وطبيعة الموقع الذي توضع فيه . أما الباب التمهيدي، فقد جعلته تحت عنوان: جذور الجدل ونشأته وتطوره عند
The practical issues? And what are these issues fundamentally? In short, we can pose the question in the following form: Is there a theory of dialectic (jadal) among the usuliyyun, and what is this theory? And does it have applications, and what are these applications? The main question I have tried to reach through the realization of a set of sub-objectives, which are: A - Gathering the theoretical and practical elements of the subject of dialectic among the usuliyyun, and forging them into a systematic structure that makes the features of the subject clear and the contributions of the usuliyyun prominent with full clarity and obviousness. B – Explaining the roots of dialectic in usuli thought, and the motives that drove the usuliyyun to excel in its use and their creativity in inventing its methods and approaches. C - Highlighting the differentiation among usuli studies regarding the use of dialectic and the strength of its appearance in these studies across their stages of emergence. D – Highlighting the role played by the dialectical method in developing the science of usul al-fiqh and enriching its topics with new discussions that appeared with the progress and development of this science. Research methodology: I have seen, considering the nature of the subject, that achieving these goals requires proceeding from foundations derived from more than one method, and these, upon a precise method that combines, the foundations are: A - History: Since this subject has a historical nature, it required me to trace the roots of dialectic in Islamic thought and the contributions of the usuliyyun in dialectical research to delving into books of history, biographies, and encyclopedias specializing in the history of books and writings, in an attempt to identify the titles of books related to the subject of dialectic attributed to their authors, then researching the biographies of these authors to determine the historical periods to which they belong, then attempting to identify the nature of the contribution made by each of them in this field. B - Induction: This foundation I used more in the theoretical aspect than in the practical aspect, and that is only because this subject suffers fundamentally from a deficiency in its theoretical aspect, so I tried to extract the theoretical foundations of the dialectical method among the usuliyyun from their actual writings in the science of usul al-fiqh, and I also applied it in the practical aspect but to a lesser extent, because the usuliyyun dealt with these applications in a number of their writings, and therefore my induction of them was a process of compilation and re-presentation of the material I collected. C - Analysis: It is the natural result of induction, for the applied scholarly material from the books of the usuliyyun led to its analysis and observation of the common elements among them, and through that I was able to determine many of the theoretical headings that this research encompasses. D - Balance between theory and practice: This is a methodological foundation that governed my research from its beginning to its end, for I tried - given the nature of the subject - to maintain this balance, and to ensure that one side of the subject does not dominate the other, and I think I succeeded in that by the grace of God Almighty, but it must be noted that the material of the subject in some positions of the research may be very scarce sometimes, and therefore I cannot maintain in this position the principle of balance; undoubtedly the nature of the subject and the nature of each of its elements and the scholarly material connected to it all have an effect in this framework. Research plan: The objectives I tried to reach and the nature of the method I followed required me to divide the subject into two main parts: one I allocate to theory, and the second to application. Since the subject strikes its roots in the depths of history and its origins are fundamentally historical, I had to allocate to the historical aspect its necessary scope in the research, but on the basis of considering it as an introduction to the research not as part of its core. Therefore, this research came divided into a preliminary section and two main sections, and each of the three sections is divided into chapters, each chapter into topics, and each topic into sub-topics, according to the type of material and the nature of the position in which it is placed. As for the preliminary section, I placed it under the title: The Roots of Dialectic, its Emergence and Development among
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is the introductory section of a research work on Jadal (dialectical reasoning) as practiced by usuliyyun (scholars of usul al-fiqh). The author begins by posing the central research question: Is there a coherent theory of jadal among usuliyyun, and what are its practical applications? He then lists four sub-objectives: (1) to gather and systematize the theoretical and practical elements of jadal, (2) to trace its roots and motives behind its use, (3) to highlight differences among usuli studies in their use of jadal, and (4) to show the role of jadal in developing usul al-fiqh. Next, the author explains his methodology, which combines four foundations: (a) historical research, involving the study of historical sources and biographies to trace the development of jadal; (b) induction (istiqra'), predominantly applied to theoretical aspects due to a perceived deficiency in theory; (c) analysis, as a natural outcome of induction, to identify common elements and theoretical headings; and (d) maintaining balance between theory and practice, acknowledging that sometimes material scarcity prevents perfect balance. Finally, the author outlines the research plan: a preliminary section on the historical roots of jadal, followed by two main sections—one on theory and one on application—each divided into chapters, topics, and sub-topics. This passage functions as a research preface, not a classical matn, and sets the framework for the entire book.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Analyzing a Research Plan in Islamic Dialectic Studies
Author outlines the research structure: a preliminary chapter and two main parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the structure of a research plan in Islamic sciences and explain how the author's divisions serve the study's goals.

Core Idea
A research plan in Islamic sciences must balance historical background with systematic theory and application.

In this passage, the author of a study on jadal (dialectic) among usuliyyin outlines his research plan. He divides his work into a preliminary chapter and two main parts: theory and application. This structure is common in Islamic scholarly works, where historical foundations are treated as an introduction, and the core is divided into theory and practice. Understanding this structure helps you evaluate the coherence of any research work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall division
Notice that the author states two main parts (theory and application) plus a preliminary chapter. List them.
The preliminary chapter is an introduction, not part of the core.
2
Examine the preliminary chapter's purpose
The author says it is a 'madkhal' (introduction) not core. It covers historical roots in Quran, Sunnah, and early generations, and development stages.
Historical background contextualizes the study.
3
Analyze the theory part's chapters
Four chapters: concept, foundations, elements, and etiquettes. Note how each builds on the previous.
Concept defines the subject, foundations provide method, elements describe procedure, etiquettes guide conduct.
4
Consider the application part
Although not detailed here, the author mentions it as the second main part. It likely applies the theoretical framework to specific debates.
Application bridges theory and practice.
5
Evaluate the plan's logical flow
Does the historical introduction lead naturally into theory? Does theory then lead to application? How does the structure support the research objectives?
A coherent plan shows clear progression.

مباحث تناولت في كل واحد منها أساسا من تلك الأسس، حيث جعلت المبحث الأول للنظر العقلي والثاني للحد أو التعريف، والثالث للاستدلال. أما الفصل الثالث الذي جعلته تحت عنوان : عناصر طريقة الجدل عند الأصوليين، الباب الأول، فجاء تحت عنوان: آداب الجدل
The research plan: The goals I sought to achieve and the nature of the methodology I followed required me to divide the subject into two main parts: one I allocate to theory, and the second to application. Since the subject has deep historical roots and its origins are fundamentally historical, it was necessary to allocate to the historical aspect its necessary scope in the research, but by way of considering it an introduction to the research, not its core. Therefore, this research came divided into a preliminary chapter and two main parts, and each of the three is divided into chapters, each chapter into sections, and each section into sub-sections, according to the type of material and the nature of the position in which it is placed. As for the preliminary chapter, I placed it under the title: 'Roots of Dialectic, Its Origin and Development among the Usuliyyin,' and I divided it into two chapters: The first chapter: 'Roots of Dialectic before the Science of Usul al-Fiqh': In its five sub-sections, I explained that this method has origins in the human psyche, its use in the Noble Qur'an and the Noble Prophetic Sunnah, and its reality in the era of the Companions and Followers, then in the era of the Followers of the Followers and the mujtahid Imams. The second chapter: I discussed the origin and development of dialectical research among the usuliyyin, and I divided it into three sub-sections according to the stages that the development of this method underwent in the books of the usuliyyin. In the first sub-section, I addressed the stage of origin and establishment; in the second, the stage of development and integration; and in the third, the stage of decline and weakness. Immediately after that comes the first part: 'The Theory of Dialectic among the Usuliyyin,' and I divided it into four chapters. In the first chapter, I addressed the concept of dialectic among the usuliyyin: in its first sub-section, I traced the meaning of jadal in the Arabic language; in the second sub-section, the definition of jadal in usuli terminology; then in the third sub-section, I studied the difference between the science of jadal and the science of munazara; and in the fourth sub-section, I also studied the difference between the science of jadal and the science of khilaf. I divided the second chapter, 'Foundations of the Dialectical Method among the Usuliyyin,' into three sub-sections, addressing in each one a foundation of those foundations: I made the first sub-section for rational consideration, the second for the definition (hadd or ta'rif), and the third for inference (istidlal). As for the third chapter, which I placed under the title 'Elements of the Dialectical Method among the Usuliyyin,' I divided it into four sub-sections: in the first, I addressed the usuliyyin's care to cover all controversial issues in usul by the dialectical method; then in the second, I addressed how dialectic proceeds practically, through question and answer; then in the third, I studied how dialectic ends, by interruption or transition; and finally, in the fourth sub-section, I addressed the result of dialectic through this method, under the title 'Fruits of Dialectic in Usul al-Fiqh.' As for the fourth and last chapter in the first part, it came under the title 'Etiquettes of Dialectic.'
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage outlines the research plan of the study. The author states that the subject is divided into two main parts: theory and application. Due to the historical nature, a preliminary chapter is included as an introduction, not core. The structure comprises a preliminary chapter and two main parts. The preliminary chapter, titled 'Roots of Dialectic, Its Origin and Development among the Usuliyyin,' has two chapters: the first covers roots before usul al-fiqh (in human psyche, Quran, Sunnah, and early generations); the second covers origin and development in three stages: establishment, development, and decline. Then comes the first main part: 'Theory of Dialectic among the Usuliyyin,' divided into four chapters. The first chapter deals with the concept of jadal (language, terminology, difference from munazara and khilaf). The second chapter covers foundations: rational consideration, definition, and inference. The third chapter covers elements: coverage of controversial issues, practical conduct (question-answer), ending (interruption/transition), and results (fruits). The fourth chapter is on etiquettes. The second main part (application) is not detailed here, likely on subsequent pages.

Introduction and Front Matter

Using a Book Outline as a Research Map in Jadal
Author presents the complete structural outline of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract the research structure of a book on Jadal Usuliyyin from its outline and identify which topics fall under theory versus application.

Core Idea
A book's outline is a research map revealing the author's methodology and priorities.

This book outline is not just a list of chapters; it is a window into how the author systematically organizes the theory and practice of jadal. Understanding this structure will help you navigate the book efficiently and grasp the logical flow of the arguments. The author first addresses historical roots, then theory, then applications to the four sources of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major divisions
Look for the two main parts (الجزء الأول and الباب الثاني) and the initial chapter (الفصل الأول, الفصل الثاني) to see the overall architecture.
The book has two parts: theory (نظرية الجدل) and applications (تطبيقات الجدل).
2
Distinguish theory from application
Notice that the first part covers concept, foundations, elements, and etiquettes; the second part covers objections to specific evidences.
3
Examine the objection structure
For each evidence type (Quran, Sunnah, Qiyas, other), the author lists specific categories of objections and responses. This shows the logical method of jadal.
For example, objections to Quranic inference include seven types like abrogation and interpretation.
4
Relate to Usul al-Fiqh
Connect each chapter to the corresponding Usul topic—e.g., the chapter on Qiyas deals with its pillars and effective cause.

نظرية الجدل عند الأصوليين، وقد قسمته إلى أربعة فصول. تناولت في الفصل الأول : مفهوم الجدل عند الأصوليين، حيث تتبعت في المبحث الأول منه معنى الجدل في اللغة العربية وفي المبحث الثاني تعريف الجدل في الاصطلاح الأصولي، ثم في المبحث الثالث درست الفرق بين علم الجدل وعلم المناظرة، وفي المبحث الرابع درست كذلك الفرق بين علم الجدل وعلم الخلاف وقسمت الفصل الثاني: أسس منهج الجدل عند الأصوليين، إلى ثلاثة مباحث تناولت في كل واحد منها أساسا من تلك الأسس، حيث جعلت المبحث الأول للنظر العقلي والثاني للحد أو التعريف، والثالث للاستدلال. أما الفصل الثالث الذي جعلته تحت عنوان : عناصر طريقة الجدل عند الأصوليين، فقسمته إلى أربعة مباحث ، تناولت في الأول منها حرص الأصوليين على استيفاء كافة المسائل الخلافية في الأصول بالطريقة الجدلية، ثم تناولت في الثاني كيفية جريان الجدل عمليّا، وذلك عبر السؤال والجواب ، ثم درست في الثالث كيفية انتهاء الجدل وذلك بالانقطاع أو الانتقال، وأخيرا تناولت في المبحث الرابع نتيجة الجدل من خلال هذه الطريقة، وذلك تحت عنوان : ثمرات الجدل في أصول الفقه . أما الفصل الرابع والأخير في الباب الأول، فجاء تحت عنوان: آداب الجدل عند الأصوليين، وقد عالجت هذه الآداب من خلال أربعة مباحث، المبحث الأول تناول : الآداب المتعلقة بشخصية المجادل، والثاني: الآداب المتعلقة بالعلاقة بين المتجادلين والثالث : الآداب المتعلقة بموضوع الجدل، والرابع: الآداب المتعلقة بأسلوب الجدل. وأما الباب الثاني : تطبيقات الجدل عند الأصوليين، فقد توصلت بالاستقراء إلى أن هذه التطبيقات تدور كلها حول الأدلة، وهي تنحصر في أربعة محاور من الأدلة : الكتاب السنة القياس، بقية الأدلة الشرعية . ولذلك درست في الفصل الأول : الجدل في الاستدلال بالكتاب، حيث حصرت الاعتراضات الواردة على الاستدلال بالآيات القرآنية والأجوبة عليها في سبعة مباحث : المبحث الأول : الاعتراض من جهة أن المستدل لا يقول بنفس الدليل المبحث الثاني: الاعتراض بالقول بموجب الآية، المبحث الثالث: الاعتراض بدعوى المشاركة في الدليل المبحث الرابع: الاعتراض باختلاف القراءات، المبحث الخامس الاعتراض بدعوى النسخ، المبحث السادس: الاعتراض من جهة التأويل المبحث السابع: الاعتراض بالمعارضة. وتناولت في الفصل الثاني الجدل في الاستدلال بالسنة (الاعتراضات الواردة عليه والأجوبة عن تلك الاعتراضات)، وذلك في أربعة مباحث: المبحث الأول : الاعتراضات على الاستدلال بالسنة من جهة الإسناد، المبحث الثاني: الاعتراضات الواردة على الاستدلال بالمتن القول المبتدأ)، المبحث الثالث : الاعتراضات على الاستدلال بالسنة الواردة على سبب المبحث الرابع: الاعتراضات الواردة على الاستدلال بأفعال النبي يا الله . أما الفصل الثالث : فخصصته للحديث عن الجدل في الاستدلال بالقياس (الاعتراضات الواردة عليه وجعلته في أربعة مباحث: المبحث الأول: الاعتراضات الواردة على الاستدلال بالقياس من جهة الحجية المبحث الثاني : الاعتراضات الواردة على عموم أركان القياس المبحث الثالث: الاعتراضات الواردة على العلة المؤثرة، المبحث الرابع: الاعتراضات الواردة على العلة الطردية . يأتي بعد ذلك الفصل الرابع والأخير من الباب الثاني والرسالة معا : الجدل في
The Jadal of the Usuliyyin, and I divided it into two chapters: The first chapter: The roots of Jadal before the science of Usul al-Fiqh: In its five sections I explained that this method has origins in the human soul, and its use in the Noble Quran, and in the Noble Prophetic Sunnah, and its reality in the era of the Companions and Followers, then in the era of the Followers of the Followers and the Mujtahid Imams. The second chapter: I dealt in it with the emergence and development of dialectical research among the Usuliyyin, and I divided it into three sections according to the stages that this method underwent in the books of the Usuliyyin: in the first section I dealt with the stage of emergence and establishment, in the second the stage of development and integration, and in the third the stage of decline and weakness. Immediately after that comes the first part: The theory of Jadal among the Usuliyyin, and I divided it into four chapters. In the first chapter I dealt with: the concept of Jadal among the Usuliyyin, where in its first section I traced the meaning of Jadal in the Arabic language, and in the second section the definition of Jadal in the Usuli terminology, then in the third section I studied the difference between the science of Jadal and the science of Munazara, and in the fourth section I also studied the difference between the science of Jadal and the science of Khilaf. And I divided the second chapter: The foundations of the method of Jadal among the Usuliyyin, into three sections, in each of which I dealt with one of those foundations, making the first section for rational consideration, the second for definition (hadd or ta'rif), and the third for inference (istidlal). As for the third chapter, which I placed under the title: Elements of the method of Jadal among the Usuliyyin, I divided it into four sections: in the first I dealt with the keenness of the Usuliyyin to cover all the disputed issues in Usul in a dialectical manner, then in the second I dealt with how Jadal proceeds practically, through question and answer, then in the third I studied how Jadal ends, by cessation or transition, and finally in the fourth section I dealt with the result of Jadal through this method, under the title: Fruits of Jadal in Usul al-Fiqh. As for the fourth and last chapter of the first part, it came under the title: Etiquettes of Jadal among the Usuliyyin, and I treated these etiquettes through four sections: the first section dealt with: the etiquettes related to the character of the disputant, the second: the etiquettes related to the relationship between the two disputants, the third: the etiquettes related to the subject of Jadal, and the fourth: the etiquettes related to the style of Jadal. As for the second part: Applications of Jadal among the Usuliyyin, I concluded by induction that these applications all revolve around the proofs, and they are confined to four axes of evidence: the Book, the Sunnah, Qiyas, and the rest of the legal proofs. Therefore, I studied in the first chapter: Jadal in inference by the Book, where I restricted the objections against inference by Quranic verses and the answers to them in seven sections: the first section: the objection from the aspect that the inferrer does not act by the same evidence, the second: the objection by saying (you must act on) the implication of the verse, the third: the objection by claiming participation in the evidence, the fourth: the objection by difference in readings, the fifth: the objection by claiming abrogation, the sixth: the objection from the aspect of interpretation, the seventh: the objection by contradiction. And I dealt in the second chapter with Jadal in inference by the Sunnah (the objections against it and the answers to those objections) in four sections: the first section: objections to inference by the Sunnah from the aspect of chain of transmission (isnad), the second: objections against inference by the text (the saying - the beginning?), the third: objections against inference by the Sunnah related to the cause, the fourth: objections against inference by the actions of the Prophet [ya Allah?]. As for the third chapter: I devoted it to discussing Jadal in inference by Qiyas (the objections against it), and I made it in four sections: the first section: objections against inference by Qiyas from the aspect of being a proof, the second: objections against the general pillars of Qiyas, the third: objections against the effective cause (al-illa al-mu'aththira), the fourth: objections against the permissive cause (al-illa al-tardiyya). After that comes the fourth and last chapter of the second part and the dissertation together: Jadal in...
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a detailed table of contents for the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin' (Dialectics of the Legal Theorists). The author outlines the entire work, which is divided into two main parts (bab) after an initial division into two chapters (fasl). The first part deals with the theory of Jadal, covering its concept, foundations, elements, etiquettes, and practical conduct. The second part deals with applications of Jadal specifically to the four sources of Islamic law: the Quran, Sunnah, Qiyas, and other proofs. Each chapter is broken down into sections (mabhath) enumerating specific types of objections and responses. The structure shows a systematic treatment of dialectical methodology as applied to Usul al-Fiqh. The author's approach is comprehensive, covering historical roots, doctrinal foundations, procedural elements, and concrete objections against each source of evidence. This outline serves as a roadmap for the entire book.

Introduction and Front Matter
advanced
10 min
Objection Typology in Jadal Applications
Author presents the complete structural outline of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize objections to legal inferences (Quran, Sunnah, Qiyas) based on the framework presented in 'Jadal Usuliyyin'.

Core Idea
Jadal objections are systematically organized by evidence type and aspect of attack.

The second part of 'Jadal Usuliyyin' provides a detailed classification of objections to the four sources of evidence. Understanding this typology is crucial for analysing real debates in Usul al-Fiqh. The author enumerates specific categories for each source, showing that jadal is not chaotic but rule-governed.

Guided Path
1
List the four evidence types
From the outline, identify the four axes: Quran, Sunnah, Qiyas, and other legal proofs.
2
For each evidence, extract objection categories
For Quran, there are 7 categories (e.g., abrogation, interpretation). For Sunnah, 4 categories (isnad, text, etc.). For Qiyas, 4 categories (proof, pillars, effective cause, permissive cause).
Note the differences in number and focus.
3
Compare objection types across evidence
Some objections are unique to certain evidence: e.g., 'difference in readings' only applies to Quran; 'chain of transmission' only to Sunnah. Others like 'contradiction' appear across multiple.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Navigating a Thesis on Jadal in Usul al-Fiqh
Author's plan and research difficulties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the organizational framework of a thesis on jadal among usuliyyin from the author's own description.

Core Idea
A thesis on jadal is structured around the sources of Islamic law and the objections raised against each.

The author's plan is more than a table of contents—it is a map of how jadal operates across different types of evidence. By examining this map, you will learn how scholars systematically approach dialectical debate in usul al-fiqh. This lesson will guide you through the author's structure and the challenges he faced, so you can appreciate the rigor required in such research.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main sections of the thesis
Read the opening lines to find the two bab (sections). The first covers adab (etiquettes) and the second covers tatbiqat (applications). Note the four sub-topics in each.
Section one has four investigations on personality, relationship, subject, and style.
2
List the four axes of evidence in the second section
The author states the applications revolve around four types of evidence: Quran, Sunna, qiyas, and other legal evidences. Confirm these in the text.
These correspond to the four chapters of the second section.
3
Map the objections for each evidence type
For each chapter, the author lists specific mabahith (investigations) that cover possible objections. Write them down and look for patterns: e.g., objections to Quranic inference are divided into seven categories.
Notice that the number of investigations varies: 7 for Quran, 4 for Sunna, 4 for qiyas, 5 for other evidences.
4
Summarize the research difficulties mentioned
The author lists four difficulties (A-D). Paraphrase each in your own words: scarcity of primary sources, pioneering nature of the work, lack of supporting references, and complexity of the subject.
Reflect on how these challenges might affect the structure or content of the thesis.

الجدل في الاستدلال بدليل الخطاب (مفهوم المخالفة) وأنهيت بعد ذلك كله هذه الرسالة بخاتمة ضمنتها النتائج التي قادني إليها البحث وكذا الآفاق التي يفتحها أمام البحث العلمي مستقبلا. الصعوبات التي اعترضت متوفرة في المكتبات العامة وقد اقتضاني الحصول على ما هو مطبوع منها انتظار وقت طويل. ب - كوني أول من يطرق الموضوع بهذه الصورة فيما أعلم وأعتقد، جعلني - كمن يدخل غابة موحشة متشابكة الأغصان دون أن يتوفر لديه دليل يريه الطريق أو له معالمها، مما جعلني أغير خطة البحث وأعدلها مرارا عديدة، ولم أستقر على خطة نهائية إلا في اللحظات الأخيرة من البحث . قلة المراجع المساعدة في المكتبات العامة ج الخاصة، جعلني
