Reasons for Iktilaf Among the Sahaba
Author discusses emergence of jadal in fiqh branches with reasons for differences in ijtihad among Sahaba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main factors that led to differences in ijtihad among the Sahaba and explain how they gave rise to the schools of hadith and opinion.

Core Idea
Jadal in fiqh arose naturally from objective factors, not mere stubbornness.

After the Prophet's death, the Sahaba faced new legal problems without direct revelation. They turned to ijtihad, and differences emerged. This lesson explores the underlying reasons—geographic variation and linguistic ambiguity—that shaped early Islamic jurisprudence and led to the formation of two major legal tendencies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the post-prophetic context
Read the opening lines and note the shift: the death of the Prophet ended direct revelation, forcing the Sahaba to rely on ijtihad for new issues.
2
Extract the first reason: geographic dispersion
Find the passage describing how companions in Syria/Hejaz versus Egypt/Iraq encountered different social pressures and had varying access to hadith scholars, leading to text-based or opinion-based fatwas.
3
Extract the second reason: textual ambiguity
Look for the examples: the word 'qur' (shared between menstruation and purity) and the word 'father' (literal vs. metaphorical for grandfather). These show how linguistic features of the Qur'an cause legitimate disagreement.
4
Connect reasons to the schools of hadith and opinion
Observe that the geographic factor produced two fatwa tendencies, which became the nuclei of the madrasatay al-ḥadīth wa al-ra’y. The textual ambiguity reinforces that even with the same text, different conclusions are possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ب - الجدل في الفروع : إلى جانب الجدل في الأمور السياسية الذي رأينا استفحاله بين الصحابة، ظهر بينهم جدل في ميدان آخر ، هو ميدان الفروع الفقهية وهذا الميدان هو الذي يهمنا أساسا في هذا البحث. ذلك أن وفاة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قد كانت إيذانا بانتهاء مرجعية الوحي التي كان الصحابة يئوبون إليها إذا ما واجهتهم مشكلة من المشكلات وأصبحوا أمام واقع جديد يطرح مشكلات جديدة لم يعرفوها من قبل ولا يعرفون في حكمها نصا من القرآن أو السنة، وقد كان طبيعيا أن يتجهوا إلى الاجتهاد بالرأي في تلك المسائل مستهدين بروح النصوص والقواعد العامة للشريعة التي تعلموها من طول صحبتهم للنبي عليه الصلاة والسلام. وما دام الأمر متعلقا بالاجتهاد بالرأي، فقد كان طبيعيًا جدًّا أن يقع بينهم الاختلاف في نتائج هذا الاجتهاد، وهذا الاختلاف - عند الاستقراء – إنما يرجع إلى أسباب واقعية وموضوعية، من أهمها : 1 - لقد كان لتفرق الصحابة في الأمصار وما واجههم من أمواج الاستفسارات عن المسائل الفقهية وأحكامها تحت وطأة العادات والأعراف الجديدة وأنماط الحياة التي لا عهد لهم بها من قبل ؛ أثره الكبير في أن تختلف فتاوى الصحابة حسب اختلاف البلاد التي يقيمون فيها من حيث مدى القرب أو البعد عن طبيعة الجزيرة العربية ومهبط الوحي والرسالة، ففتاوى الصحابة الذين يقيمون بالشام والحجاز كانت أقرب إلى الانضباط الحرفي بالنصوص الثابتة في الكتاب أو السنة، وأبعد ما تكون - جهد الاستطاعة عن الرأي والاجتهاد المرسل، إذ العادات الطارئة والغريبة فيما بينهم كانت قليلة، ولم تكن من الكثرة بحيث تفيض عما تتسع له دائرة النصوص من الفتاوى والأحكام وبالمقابل، فقد كان فيهم أعداد وفيرة من علماء السنة وحفاظها. أما فتاوى الصحابة المقيمين في مصر والعراق، فقد كانت أقرب إلى الاجتهاد المرسل والاعتماد على البصيرة والرأي وأبعد - في كثير من المسائل والأحكام عن الانضباط بالدلالات المباشرة من النصوص، إذ كانت العادات الطارئة ومظاهر المدنية الغريبة عن مألوفاتهم في تلك البلاد أكثر وأوسع، إلى جانب أن علماء السنة وحفاظ الحديث هناك كانوا أقل كثرة وأضعف دراية وحفظًا. وقد ظهر نتيجة لذلك الاختلاف بين تلك البلاد لونان من الفتاوى؛ أحدهما مصطبغ بالرأي آخذ بأطراف كثيرة منه - جهد الاستطاعة - والثاني متقيد بالنصوص، مبتعد عن تحكيم الرأي والاعتماد عليه (1)، وقد كان ذلك نواة مدرستي الحديث والرأي اللتين استفحل أمرهما فيما بعد. 2 - ومن هذه الأسباب أيضًا؛ اختلافهم في فهم القرآن، لأن دلالة آياته ليست قطعية كلها، بل كثير منها ظني الدلالة، إما بسبب لفظ مشترك بين معنيين فيحمله واحد على أحد المعنيين، بينما يحمله الآخر على المعنى الثاني لقرينة تظهر له، كما في قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَالْمُطَلَّقَاتُ يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ ثَلَثَةَ قُرُو ... ﴾ (2) ، والقرء في اللغة مشترك بين الحيض والطهر ، فحمله بعضهم على الحيض وقال عدتها ثلاث حيض، وآخرون على الطهر، وقالوا عدتها ثلاثة أطهار . وإما بسبب لفظ اختلف فيه ؛ هل هو حقيقة أو مجاز؟ كاختلافهم في أن الجد يحجب الإخوة من الميراث كالأب؟ فذهب أبو بكر إلى ذلك لأن القرآن سماه أبا : ﴿ وَاتَّبَعْتُ مِلَّةَ آبَائِي إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْحَاقَ وَيَعْقُوبَ ﴾ (3).
B - Jadal in legal branches: Alongside jadal in political affairs which we have seen becoming rampant among the companions, there appeared among them jadal in another field, which is the field of fiqh branches, and this field is the one that concerns us fundamentally in this research. That is because the death of the Prophet, peace be upon him, signaled the end of the reference of revelation to which the companions used to resort when faced with a problem, and they faced a new reality presenting new problems that they had not known before and for whose ruling they knew no text from the Qur'an or Sunnah. It was natural that they turned to ijtihad by opinion in those matters, guided by the spirit of the texts and the general rules of Shari'a that they had learned from their long companionship with the Prophet, peace be upon him. And since the matter is related to ijtihad by opinion, it was very natural that difference occurred among them in the results of this ijtihad. This difference - upon induction - is due to real and objective reasons, the most important of which are: 1. The dispersion of the companions in various regions and the waves of inquiries about fiqh matters and their rulings under the pressure of new customs, traditions, and lifestyles that they had no previous acquaintance with had a great effect in causing the fatwas of the companions to differ according to the difference of the countries they resided in, in terms of proximity or distance from the nature of the Arabian Peninsula and the place of revelation and the message. Thus, the fatwas of the companions residing in Syria and Hejaz were closer to literal adherence to the established texts in the Book or Sunnah, and as far as possible - by effort - from opinion and unfettered ijtihad, since the novel and strange customs among them were few, and not so numerous as to overflow what the scope of texts could accommodate in terms of fatwas and rulings. Conversely, among them were abundant numbers of scholars of the Sunnah and its memorizers. As for the fatwas of the companions residing in Egypt and Iraq, they were closer to unfettered ijtihad and reliance on insight and opinion, and further - in many matters and rulings - from adherence to the direct indications of the texts, since the novel customs and manifestations of civilization strange to their norms in those countries were more and broader, along with the fact that the scholars of Sunnah and memorizers of hadith there were fewer in number and weaker in knowledge and memorization. Consequently, as a result of that difference between those countries, two colors of fatwas emerged: one tinged with opinion, taking many of its aspects - as much as possible - and the second restricted to texts, distant from subjecting to opinion and relying on it. And that was the nucleus of the two schools of hadith and opinion that later became rampant. 2. And among these reasons also is their difference in understanding the Qur'an, because the indication of its verses is not all definitive; rather many of them are probable in indication, either due to a word shared between two meanings, so one may carry it to one of the meanings while another carries it to the other meaning due to a contextual indication that appears to him, as in His saying, may He be exalted: 'And divorced women shall wait concerning themselves for three quru.' And 'qur' in language is shared between menstruation and purity. So some carried it to menstruation and said her waiting period is three menstruations, and others to purity and said her waiting period is three periods of purity. Or due to a word disputed over whether it is literal or metaphorical, like their difference over whether the grandfather excludes the siblings from inheritance like the father? So Abu Bakr held that because the Qur'an called him father: 'And I follow the religion of my fathers Ibrahim, Ishaq, and Ya'qub.' (Surah Yusuf: 38).
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This lengthy passage introduces the second type of jadal among the companions: jadal in legal branches (furū‘ fiqhiyya). The author explains that after the Prophet's death, the companions faced new problems without direct texts, so they turned to ijtihad by opinion. Differences naturally emerged, and two objective reasons are given. First, the geographic dispersion: companions in Syria and Hejaz (closer to the birthplace of Islam) encountered fewer new customs and had more hadith scholars, so they adhered more literally to texts. Those in Egypt and Iraq faced more novel situations and had fewer hadith specialists, leading to more opinion-based fatwas. This gave rise to the two schools: school of hadith and school of opinion. Second, differences in understanding the Qur'an due to polysemy (e.g., ‘qur’ meaning menstruation or purity) and disputes over literal vs. metaphorical meaning (e.g., the word ‘father’ applied to grandfather in inheritance). The passage uses the example of the word 'qur' in verse 2:228 and the disagreement over whether the grandfather is like the father in inheriting, citing Abu Bakr's opinion based on Quranic usage. This illustrates how textual ambiguity leads to jadal. The passage sets the stage for the author's focus on legal jadal.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Historical Roots of Jadal: Tabi'in Period
Historical overview of the Tabi'in period showing how debates arose from conflicting juristic methodologies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the historical factors that led to the emergence of jadal between the School of Hadith and the School of Opinion in the Tabi'in period.

Core Idea
Jadal emerged from real historical factors: the spread of Sahaba and distinct regional methodologies.

This lesson traces the origin of jadal (dialectical debate) in Islamic jurisprudence to the Tabi'in period. The geographical dispersal of the Companions created distinct juristic methodologies in Medina and Iraq, setting the stage for methodological conflict that would define early Islamic legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the effect of Sahaba dispersal
Notice how the passage describes the Companions spreading across regions, each carrying unique knowledge. This naturally led to different methodological emphases in each region.
The dispersal is the primary historical cause of later jadal.
2
Contrast the two regional methodologies
Contrast the Hijazi approach (Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab) which relied on hadith and consensus, with the Iraqi approach (Ibrahim al-Nakha'i) which used qiyas and independent reasoning. Identify the key figures and their sources.
These represent the seeds of the School of Hadith and School of Opinion.
3
Identify the link to jadal
The passage states that the diversity evolved into 'open conflict' characterized by disputes over the validity of ra'y. This conflict is the historical context for the practice of jadal.
Jadal became a tool to resolve or manage these methodological disagreements.

المطلب الثاني : الجدل في عصر التابعين
تربى فقهاء التابعين تحت رعاية من سبقوهم من الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم، وأخذوا عنهم العلم والفقه، وقد حدث ذلك حين انتشر الصحابة في أمصار الدولة الإسلامية وتنقلوا إليها لتعليم الناس أمور دينهم، وقد أنشأوا حركة علمية في كل مصر نزلوا فيه، ولدى كل واحد منهم من العلم ما قد لا يكون لدى الآخر، وكونوا مدارس منهجية في تعليمهم وكان لهم تلاميذ ينقلون عنهم العلم، فتخرج عليهم التابعون ونهجوا في العلم مناهجهم وهؤلاء هم اضطلعوا بما كان يضطلع به علماء وفقهاء الصحابة من اجتهاد وفتوى وقضاء يقول ابن القيم رحمه الله : «والدين والفقه انتشرا في الأمة عن طريق أصحاب ابن مسعود وأصحاب زيد بن ثابت وأصحاب عبد الله بن عمر وأصحاب عبد الله بن عباس، فعلم الناس عامته عن أصحاب هؤلاء الأربعة، أما أهل المدينة فعلمهم أصحاب زيد بن ثابت وعبد الله بن عمر، وأما أهل مكة فعلمهم من أصحاب عبد الله بن مسعود». أثر انتشار الصحابة في اختلاف مناهج التابعين : ولقد كان من نتائج انتشار الصحابة وتفرقهم على الأمصار، وكذا تفقه أهل كل مصر على من حل بينهم من الصحابة ؛ أن تأثر أهل كل مصر بمناهج الصحابة الذين نزلوا فيه في استنباط الأحكام واستفادتها من مظانها . وكان من الطبيعي أن يلتزم أهل كل مصر من تلك الأمصار بما وصل إليهم عن طريق فقهائهم ومعلميهم من الصحابة رضي الله عنهم وتقديمهم على غيرهم، لذلك وجدنا سعيد بن المسيب وأصحابه كانوا يرون أن علماء الحرمين الشريفين أثبت الناس في الحديث والفقه، ولذلك جمع فتاوى أبي بكر وعمر وعثمان وأحكامهم، وفتاوى علي قبل الخلافة وعائشة وابن عباس وابن عمر وزيد بن ثابت وأبي هريرة، وقد اعتمد ابن المسيب مسند أبي هريرة كثيرا وقضايا قضاة المدينة وحفظ من ذلك شيئًا كثيرًا، ونظر فيها نظر اعتبار وتفتيش وتحقيق وتطبيق، فما كان مجمعًا عليه بين علماء المدينة عض عليه بالنواجذ هو وأصحابه لا يتجاوزونه . ومن الجانب الآخر في العراق كان إبراهيم النخعي وأصحابه يرون أن عبد الله بن مسعود أثبت في الفقه ... كما أخذ إبراهيم بفتاوى علي وأحكامه مدة خلافته بالكوفة، وأبي موسى الأشعري، وسعد بن أبي وقاص، وقضايا شريح، إذ كان يستشير فيها عمر وعثمان، فعمل إبراهيم في آثار هؤلاء مثلما عمل سعيد في آثار أهل المدينة، وخرج على فقههم بالقياس والاستنباط فيما لم ينصوا فيه واتخذ قضاياهم أصلا له فكان سعيد بن المسيب لسان فقهاء المدينة والمخطط لبنائهم، وكان إبراهيم لسان العراقيين والمؤسس لمذهبهم . ظهور مدرسة الرأي ومدرسة الحديث ونشأة الجدل بينهما : ولقد تطور ذلك التنوع في الرأي واختلاف النظرة إلى مصادر الأحكام ومواردها ليتحول إلى نزاع ظاهر تميز به هذا العصر كان يشتد بين فقهاء الحجاز وفقهاء العراق في الأخذ بالرأي فمدرسة أهل الرأي التي نشأت بالعراق قد تميزت بكثرة التفريع للفروع لكثرة ما يعرض لهم من الحوادث، بل وحتى فرضها قبل وقوعها في كثير من الأحيان، كما تميزت أيضًا بقلة روايتهم للحديث واشتراطهم فيه شروطا لا يسلم معها إلا القليل
The Second Topic: Dialectic in the Era of the Followers. The jurists of the Followers were raised under the care of those who preceded them from the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, and they took knowledge and jurisprudence from them. That occurred when the Companions spread throughout the regions of the Islamic state and moved to them to teach people their religious affairs. They established a scholarly movement in every region they settled in, and each one of them possessed knowledge that others might not have. They created systematic schools in their teaching and had students who transmitted knowledge from them. Thus the Followers graduated under them and followed their methodologies in knowledge. These are the ones who undertook the same tasks as the scholars and jurists of the Companions, including ijtihad, fatwa, and judiciary. Ibn al-Qayyim, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'Religion and jurisprudence spread in the ummah through the companions of Ibn Mas'ud, the companions of Zayd ibn Thabit, the companions of Abdullah ibn Umar, and the companions of Abdullah ibn Abbas. The general knowledge of the people comes from the companions of these four. As for the people of Medina, they were taught by the companions of Zayd ibn Thabit and Abdullah ibn Umar. As for the people of Mecca, they were taught by the companions of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud.' The effect of the spread of the Companions on the differing methodologies of the Followers: Among the consequences of the spread and dispersal of the Companions across the regions, and the fact that the people of each region learned from the Companions who settled among them, was that the people of each region were influenced by the methodologies of the Companions who settled there in deriving rulings and obtaining them from their sources. It was natural that the people of each region adhered to what reached them through their jurists and teachers from the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, and gave them precedence over others. Therefore we found Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and his companions believed that the scholars of the two noble sanctuaries (Mecca and Medina) were the most established in hadith and jurisprudence. For that reason he collected the fatwas of Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman and their rulings, and the fatwas of Ali before his caliphate, Aisha, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, Zayd ibn Thabit, and Abu Hurayra. Ibn al-Musayyab relied heavily on the musnad of Abu Hurayra and the judgments of the judges of Medina. He memorized a great deal of that and examined them with consideration, investigation, verification, and application. Whatever was agreed upon among the scholars of Medina, he and his companions held onto it firmly and did not go beyond it. On the other side in Iraq, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and his companions believed that Abdullah ibn Mas'ud was the most established in jurisprudence... Likewise, Ibrahim adopted the fatwas of Ali and his rulings during his caliphate in Kufa, and those of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, and the judgments of Shurayh, since Umar and Uthman would consult him. Thus Ibrahim worked on the traditions of these individuals just as Sa'id worked on the traditions of the people of Medina. He derived from their jurisprudence through qiyas and inference in matters on which they had not explicitly ruled, and he took their judgments as a basis. So Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab was the spokesman of the jurists of Medina and the planner of their structure, while Ibrahim was the spokesman of the Iraqis and the founder of their school. The emergence of the School of Opinion and the School of Hadith and the birth of dialectic between them: This diversity in opinion and differing views on the sources and resources of rulings developed into an apparent conflict that characterized this era, which intensified between the jurists of Hijaz and the jurists of Iraq regarding the adoption of ra'y. The School of Opinion that arose in Iraq was characterized by extensive branching of subsidiary issues due to the many incidents that occurred to them, and even their hypothetical assumption in many cases. It was also characterized by their few hadith narrations and their stipulation of conditions that allowed only a few narrations to pass.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative from a modern study on the development of jadal (dialectic) in Islamic jurisprudence. It begins by explaining how the Tabi'in (Followers) inherited knowledge from the Sahaba (Companions), who had spread across the Islamic empire, each region having its own set of teachers. The author quotes Ibn al-Qayyim to highlight the key four groups of Sahaba who were the main sources: the companions of Ibn Mas'ud, Zayd ibn Thabit, Abdullah ibn Umar, and Abdullah ibn Abbas. This geographical dispersal naturally led to different methodological emphases. The passage then gives two concrete examples: Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab in Medina, who prioritized the consensus of Medinan scholars and collected the fatwas of the early caliphs and prominent Sahaba, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i in Iraq, who followed Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and relied on qiyas (analogical reasoning) and inference. These two figures represent the seeds of what would become the School of Hadith (Medina) and the School of Opinion (Iraq). Finally, the passage describes how this diversity evolved into open conflict, with the Iraqi school characterized by extensive hypothetical rulings and fewer hadith narrations due to strict criteria. This sets the stage for the practice of jadal (dialectical debate) as a tool for juristic disagreement.

التابعون
الجدل
مدرسة الرأي
مدرسة الحديث

Six Factors Shaping Early Islamic Legal Theory
Author enumerates six factors that intensified juristic disagreements after the Companions' era.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six factors that intensified juristic disagreements after the Companions and explain how each contributed to the development of distinct usul methodologies.

Core Idea
The diversity of Islamic legal theory was systematically shaped by historical, political, and social factors, not by arbitrary differences.

Early Muslim jurists disagreed not merely about specific rulings but about the very methods of deriving them. This lesson identifies six concrete factors that deepened these methodological divides and led to the emergence of distinct regional schools such as the Medinan and Iraqi traditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contrasting schools
The passage contrasts ahl al-hadith (Medina) and ahl al-ra'y (Iraq). Note their core attitudes: one cautious about speculation, the other embraces reasoning.
2
List the six factors
Scan the passage for the numbered list. Write them down: (1) delving into hidden meanings, (2) differences in handling Sunnah due to sects, (3) impossibility of ijma', (4) proliferation of hadith narration, (5) fabrication of hadith, (6) new problems without texts.
These are explicitly enumerated in the Arabic text.
3
See how each factor leads to methodological distinctiveness
For each factor, ask: How did this push scholars toward a particular approach? For example, the impossibility of ijma' meant each region leaned on its own consensus.
Consider how factor 3 directly contributed to the Medinan reliance on local consensus.
4
Trace the regional outcomes
Notice that Medinans adopted ijma' of Medina, Iraqis adopted qiyas. Also note that Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i exemplify these trends.
The passage explicitly mentions these two figures as representatives.
5
Synthesize the overall impact
The passage concludes that these factors multiplied usul methodologies and clarified rules, leading to distinct regional schools. Reflect on how this historical process shaped the later discipline of usul al-fiqh.

أما مدرسة أهل الحديث التي نشأت بالحجاز وفي المدينة المنورة خصوصا، فقد تميزت بكراهية السؤال وفرض المسائل وتشعيب القضايا، وكذا الاعتداد بالحديث والوقوف عند الآثار، وقد اشتد النقاش العلمي بين المدرستين وعقدت المناظرات، وقام الجدل على قدم وساق وطعن كل منهما بالآخر وعاب طريقته وتشكك فيما وصل إليه من أحكام، وكان كل إمام أو مجتهد أو مناظر يحاول أن يدعم رأيه بالأدلة والبراهين العلمية والعقلية. ج - عوامل جديدة زادت من حدة الاختلاف : ومما زاد من حدة الاختلاف وتوسيع شقته في هذا العهد أكثر من ذي قبل وبروز الاختلافات في الاجتهاد ومناهج الاستنباط وفي الأحكام والفتاوى ؛ ظهور عوامل جديدة ميزت هذا العهد عما سبقه، ومن هذه العوامل : افتتان الناس في هذا العهد بالغوص على المعاني والتعمق فيما وراء النصوص، ومن الطبيعي أن ينشأ ذلك الاختلاف فيما يتوصلون إليه من نظرا لتباين أفكارهم وخلفياتهم الفكرية وتنوع مدارسهم بين أهل الرأي وأهل الحديث. 2 - اختلاف طرقهم في الأخذ بالسنة ، فإنه نتيجة للاختلافات السياسية وظهور الفرق المذهبية والكلامية من شيعة وخوارج ؛ اختلفت مواقفهم من السنة ومن العمل بها . 3 - تعذر تحقق الإجماع، نظرا لحدوث الفرقة ولأن كل فرقة سحبت ثقتها من سائر علماء الفرق الأخرى، فلم تعد تعتد بشيء من قولهم وافقوا أو خالفوا. 4 - شيوع رواية الأحاديث والسنن بعد أن لم تكن كذلك. 5 - ظهور حركة الوضع في الأحاديث. 6 - بروز قضايا ومشكلات جديدة، وتفتح العقل على أمور لم يرد فيها نص من القرآن الكريم أو السنة النبوية، كما لم تكن تلك الأمور مطروحة من قبل على العقل المسلم فلم يترك الصحابة فيها رأيًا، فاتسع الاجتهاد وتنوعت مناهجه. إن استفحال هذه العوامل الجديدة وطروها على المجتمع الإسلامي بعد عهد الصحابة، أدى إلى تميز مناهج وطرق العلماء في الاستنباط وكذا توضح القواعد المستند إليها فيه حيث كان لكل بلد علماؤه وفقهاؤه وكانت مناهجهم تلك تنمو وتزداد وضوحًا كلما تقدم بهم الزمن . وهذا بدوره ضاعف مادة المناهج الأصولية، وساعد على إبرازها في قواعد وضوابط يتبناها أهل كل مصر، فأهل المدينة أصبحوا يعتمدون على إجماع فقهاء المدينة، فأضافوا بذلك إلى الأدلة الشرعية دليلًا جديدًا هو إجماع فقهاء بلدهم. كما وجد فقهاء العراق في القياس مصدرًا ثرا لاستخراج الأحكام فيما لم يرد فيه نص من كتاب أو سنة أو أثر عن الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم؛ إذ كانوا يرون أن أحكام الشرع معقولة المعنى مشتملة على مصالح راجعة إلى الأمة وأنها بنيت على أصول محكمة، وعلل ضابطة لتلك الأحكام فهمت من الكتاب والسنة وشرعت الأحكام لأجلها لينتظم بها أمر الحياة، فكانوا يجتهدون في معرفتها لإدارة الحكم لأجلها حيثما دارت. وقد تبلورت بعض القواعد الأصولية أيضًا في هذا العهد «فسعيد بن المسيب مثلا كان يرى المصلحة في الاستنباط عند فقد النص، بينما كان إبراهيم النخعي يعتمد على القياس، فيستخرج العلة في المسألة التي ورد فيها نص ويطبقها على الفروع وينقل حكم النص إلى تلك الفروع» كما ظهر في هذا العهد أيضًا من القواعد الأصولية، الاحتجاج بقول الصحابي . وهكذا نجد أن علماء كل بلد وفقهاءه كانت لهم مناهج وطرق في الاستنباط
As for the school of hadith that arose in the Hijaz and especially in Medina, it was characterized by dislike of questioning, imposing issues, and fragmenting cases, as well as relying on hadith and adhering to traditions. The scientific debate between the two schools intensified, debates were held, and argumentation became vigorous; each criticized the other, objected to its method, and doubted the rulings it reached. Every imam, mujtahid, or debater tried to support his opinion with scientific and rational evidence and proofs. C - New factors that increased the intensity of disagreement: Among what increased the intensity of disagreement and widened its scope in this era more than before, and the emergence of differences in ijtihad, methods of deduction, rulings, and fatwas, was the appearance of new factors that distinguished this era from what preceded it. Some of these factors are: the fascination of people in this era with delving into meanings and going deeply into what is beyond texts. Naturally, this led to differences in what they arrived at due to the diversity of their ideas, intellectual backgrounds, and the variety of their schools between the people of opinion and the people of hadith. 2 - The difference in their methods of taking the Sunnah, for it was a result of political differences and the emergence of sectarian and theological factions such as Shi'a and Khawarij; their positions regarding the Sunnah and acting upon it differed. 3 - The impossibility of achieving consensus, due to the occurrence of division and because each faction withdrew its trust from the scholars of other factions, so they no longer considered any of their statements, whether they agreed or disagreed. 4 - The widespread narration of hadiths and sunnas after they were not like that. 5 - The emergence of the fabrication movement in hadiths. 6 - The emergence of new issues and problems, and the mind opening up to matters for which there is no text from the Qur'an or the Sunnah, and such matters were not previously presented to the Muslim mind, so the Companions left no opinion on them. Thus ijtihad expanded and its methods diversified. The prevalence of these new factors and their emergence in Islamic society after the era of the Companions led to the distinction of the methods and ways of the scholars in deduction, as well as the clarification of the rules relied upon therein, as each region had its scholars and jurists, and their methods grew and became clearer over time. This in turn multiplied the material of usul methodologies and helped in presenting them as rules and controls adopted by the people of each region. Thus the people of Medina began to rely on the consensus of the jurists of Medina, so they added a new proof to the legal proofs, namely the consensus of the jurists of their region. Likewise, the jurists of Iraq found in qiyas a rich source for deriving rulings in matters for which there is no text from the Book, Sunnah, or companion precedent; for they held that the rulings of Sharia are intelligible in meaning, include benefits returning to the community, and are built upon solid foundations and controlling causes for those rulings, understood from the Book and Sunnah, and the rulings were legislated for their sake to regulate the affairs of life. So they would strive to know them in order to apply the ruling for them wherever they were found. Some usul rules also crystallized in this era: 'Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, for example, saw maslaha in deduction when text was absent, while Ibrahim al-Nakha'i relied on qiyas, extracting the cause in an issue from which a text exists and applying it to branches and transferring the ruling of the text to those branches.' Also in this era, another usul rule emerged: the argument from the statement of a companion. Thus we find that the scholars and jurists of each region had their own methods and ways in deduction.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a historical account of the factors that increased disagreement among Muslim jurists after the generation of the Companions. The author begins by contrasting the two main schools: the school of hadith in Medina, which was cautious about speculative questioning and relied heavily on transmitted traditions, and the school of opinion (ahl al-ra'y) which emerged in Iraq and elsewhere. The passage then lists six specific factors: (1) the trend of delving deeply into meanings beyond the texts; (2) differences in methods of dealing with the Sunnah due to political and sectarian divisions; (3) the impossibility of achieving consensus because each sect no longer recognized the authority of others; (4) the proliferation of hadith narration after it had been scarce; (5) the emergence of fabricated hadiths; and (6) the rise of new issues not addressed by explicit texts or companion opinions. The author then explains how these factors led to the development of distinct regional methodologies: the Medinan school emphasized the consensus of Medina's jurists as a source of law, while the Iraqi school relied heavily on analogical reasoning (qiyas) because they believed that legal rulings are grounded in intelligible causes and public interests. The passage concludes by noting that both Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib (representing the Medinan approach) and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (representing the Iraqi approach) developed specific usul rules, and that the statement of a companion also emerged as a distinct source. The overall argument is that the diversity of Islamic legal methodology was not arbitrary but was shaped by concrete historical and social circumstances.

أهل الحديث
أهل الرأي
الإجماع
القياس

Historical Factors Behind Methodological Diversity and the Rise of Jadal
Author traces historical factors leading to diversity in Islamic legal methodology and the rise of jadal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key historical factors that led to methodological diversity in usul al-fiqh and explain how these factors gave rise to jadal.

Core Idea
Methodological diversity emerged because new problems required new solutions, and each region developed its own tools.

The passage explains why Islamic legal methodology became diverse after the Companions' era. New issues arose that were not covered by explicit texts, forcing jurists to develop their own methods of ijtihad. This diversity led naturally to jadal (dialectical debate) about the very principles of methodology. Understanding this historical background is crucial for grasping why jadal became an essential part of usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger
What new situation after the Companions forced jurists to innovate? Look for the mention of 'new issues and problems' and lack of textual precedent.
2
Compare the two regional schools
Contrast the Madinan school's reliance on regional ijma' with the Iraqi school's reliance on qiyas. Note the underlying rationale given for each.
3
Analyze the stance of specific jurists
Consider Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib (Madinan, using maslaha) and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (Iraqi, using qiyas). How do they exemplify broader regional tendencies?
4
Connect to jadal
Why does the author state that debate about these rules was inevitable? Identify the link between methodological divergence and the emergence of jadal.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
6 - بروز قضايا ومشكلات جديدة، وتفتح العقل على أمور لم يرد فيها نص من القرآن الكريم أو السنة النبوية، كما لم تكن تلك الأمور مطروحة من قبل على العقل المسلم فلم يترك الصحابة فيها رأيًا، فاتسع الاجتهاد وتنوعت مناهجه. إن استفحال هذه العوامل الجديدة وطروها على المجتمع الإسلامي بعد عهد الصحابة، أدى إلى تميز مناهج وطرق العلماء في الاستنباط وكذا توضح القواعد المستند إليها فيه حيث كان لكل بلد علماؤه وفقهاؤه وكانت مناهجهم تلك تنمو وتزداد وضوحًا كلما تقدم بهم الزمن . وهذا بدوره ضاعف مادة المناهج الأصولية، وساعد على إبرازها في قواعد وضوابط يتبناها أهل كل مصر، فأهل المدينة أصبحوا يعتمدون على إجماع فقهاء المدينة، فأضافوا بذلك إلى الأدلة الشرعية دليلاً جديدًا هو إجماع فقهاء بلدهم. كما وجد فقهاء العراق في القياس مصدرًا ثريًا لاستخراج الأحكام فيما لم يرد فيه نص من كتاب أو سنة أو أثر عن الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم؛ إذ كانوا يرون أن أحكام الشرع معقولة المعنى مشتملة على مصالح راجعة إلى الأمة وأنها بنيت على أصول محكمة، وعلل ضابطة لتلك الأحكام فهمت من الكتاب والسنة وشرعت الأحكام لأجلها لينتظم بها أمر الحياة، فكانوا يجتهدون في معرفتها لإدارة الحكم لأجلها حيثما دارت. وقد تبلورت بعض القواعد الأصولية أيضًا في هذا العهد «فسعيد بن المسيب مثلاً كان يرى المصلحة في الاستنباط عند فقد النص، بينما كان إبراهيم النخعي يعتمد على القياس، فيستخرج العلة في المسألة التي ورد فيها نص ويطبقها على الفروع وينقل حكم النص إلى تلك الفروع» كما ظهر في هذا العهد أيضًا من القواعد الأصولية، الاحتجاج بقول الصحابي . وهكذا نجد أن علماء كل بلد وفقهاءه كانت لهم مناهج وطرق في الاستنباط تنمو وتزداد وضوحًا كلما تقدم بهم الزمن، ولقد كان طبيعياً وبديهياً أن يدور الجدل والنقاش في هذه القواعد ذاتها، لأنها هي السبب الأساس للاختلاف في الفروع التي تنبني عليها
6 - The emergence of new issues and problems, and the opening of the mind to matters for which there is no text from the Noble Qur'an or the Prophetic Sunnah, and those matters were not previously presented to the Muslim mind so the Companions did not leave an opinion on them, thus ijtihad expanded and its methods diversified. Indeed, the intensification of these new factors and their emergence in Islamic society after the era of the Companions led to the distinction of the methods and ways of scholars in deduction as well as the clarification of the rules upon which it is based, for each country had its scholars and jurists, and their methods grew and became clearer as time progressed. This in turn multiplied the material of the methodological principles and helped to highlight them in rules and controls adopted by the people of each region. So the people of Madinah came to rely on the consensus of the jurists of Madinah, thus adding to the legal evidences a new evidence: the consensus of the jurists of their city. Likewise, the jurists of Iraq found in analogy a rich source for extracting rulings regarding matters for which there is no text from the Book, Sunnah, or tradition from the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them; for they held that the rulings of the Law are reasonable in meaning, containing benefits returning to the community, and that they are built upon solid foundations and controlling causes for those rulings understood from the Book and Sunnah, and the rulings were legislated for their sake so that the order of life might be regulated by them. So they exerted effort to know them in order to apply the ruling for their sake wherever they were found. Some methodological principles also crystallized in this era: 'Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, for example, saw benefit in deduction when the text was absent, while Ibrahim al-Nakha'i relied on analogy, extracting the cause in the issue for which a text existed and applying it to branches, transferring the ruling of the text to those branches.' Also in this era appeared among the methodological principles the argument from the statement of a Companion. Thus we find that the scholars and jurists of each country had their methods and ways of deduction that grew and became clearer as time progressed, and it was natural and obvious that debate and discussion would revolve around these very rules, because they are the primary cause of disagreement in the branches that are built upon them.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is an introductory historical analysis explaining the rise of methodological diversity in Islamic legal theory (usul al-fiqh) and its connection to the emergence of jadal (dialectical debate). The author begins by identifying the key factor: after the era of the Companions, new issues arose for which no explicit Qur'anic or Prophetic text existed, and the Companions had not expressed any opinion. This necessitated ijtihad (independent reasoning), and the methods of ijtihad varied from region to region. The author then notes that these methods grew and became more defined over time, leading to the formation of distinct schools of legal methodology. Two major examples are given: the school of Madinah, which adopted the consensus (ijma') of the Madinan jurists as an additional source of law, and the school of Iraq, which relied on qiyas (analogical reasoning) as a rich source for deriving rulings where no text existed. The Iraqi jurists viewed legal rulings as intelligible, based on underlying causes ('illal) and purposes (masalih), which they sought to understand and apply. The passage then mentions specific early jurists: Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib (Medinan) who prioritized maslaha (public interest) in the absence of text, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (Iraqi) who used qiyas to extend rulings from a textual case to analogous branches. Another principle that emerged was the authority of a Companion's statement. The author concludes by stating that it was inevitable that jadal (debate) would arise concerning these very methodological rules, since they are the root cause of divergence in derivative rulings. The passage thus sets the stage for the study of jadal in usul al-fiqh, grounding it in historical reality.

Key Terms
الجدل
القياس
الإجماع
المصلحة
العلة

The Origins of Jadal Usuli with al-Shafi'i
Author states that jadal usuli began together with usul al-fiqh by al-Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the historical connection between the codification of usul al-fiqh and the emergence of jadal usuli.

Core Idea
Jadal usuli was born with the very codification of usul al-fiqh.

This passage establishes a crucial historical fact: the discipline of usul al-fiqh and the dialectical debate about its principles (jadal usuli) began together. Understanding this connection helps us see that jadal usuli is not an afterthought but an integral part of usul al-fiqh from its inception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key figure and his contribution
The author points to Imam al-Shafi'i as the one who began the systematic writing of usul al-fiqh. Note that this is a standard historical claim.
Al-Shafi'i's al-Risala is considered the first work on usul al-fiqh.
2
Understand the claim of simultaneity
The passage says that with the codification, effects of contemporary debates were carried along, and actual research in jadal usuli also began.
The Arabic uses 'استصحب معه آثار' (brought with it the effects).
3
Reflect on the implication
If jadal usuli began with the science itself, then dialectical debate is inherent to usul al-fiqh, not a later addition.
4
Connect to the promise of elaboration
The author says he will show more in the next chapter, so this is a forward-looking statement.
The phrase 'كما سنبين في الفصل الموالي' indicates a preview.

Three Stages of Jadal Usuli Development
Author divides the historical development of jadal usuli into three stages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and describe the three historical stages of jadal usuli as outlined by the author, and explain how jadal usuli originated alongside usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Jadal usuli began with al-Shafi'i's Risala and passed through three stages: foundation, flourishing, and decline.

In this preface, the author sets the stage for a detailed examination of jadal usuli (dialectical debate in usul al-fiqh). He reviews the intense juristic disagreements among early Muslims and explains that these disagreements moved from furu' (branches) to usul (principles), prompting the need for a systematic methodology. Crucially, he argues that jadal usuli research was born with the science of usul al-fiqh itself, as exemplified by al-Shafi'i's al-Risala. The author then proposes a three-phase historical trajectory for this discipline, which provides a framework for understanding its rise and fall.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject matter
The author is describing the historical development of jadal usuli. Notice that he begins by establishing the context of jurisprudential disagreement and then connects it to the emergence of usul al-fiqh and jadal usuli together.
2
Locate the key turning point
Find where the author states the beginning of jadal usuli. He explicitly says it started with al-Shafi'i's al-Risala, which also marks the beginning of usul al-fiqh as a codified discipline.
This simultaneity is a central claim of the passage.
3
Extract the three stages
List the three stages in order: (1) emergence and foundation, (2) development and integration, (3) decline and weakness. Note the time boundaries: stage 2 ends at the beginning of the 7th century AH; stage 3 ends in the 10th century AH.
4
Understand the criterion
Each stage is defined by the state of research in jadal usuli: initial formation, then flourishing, then regressing until it ceased. The author uses qualitative descriptors (brightest days, luster faded).
5
Evaluate the author's admission
The author admits that drawing precise lines between stages is very difficult. This highlights the organic nature of intellectual history and warns against oversimplification.
Think about why boundaries are blurry: continuity of scholarship, overlapping periods, etc.

توطئة : الفصل الثاني نشأة وتطور البحث الجدلي عند الأصوليين عصر أتباع انتهينا في الفصل السابق إلى أن الخلاف الفقهي كان قد احتدم في التابعين والأئمة المجتهدين، وهذا الخلاف لم يتوقف عند الفروع، بل تعداه منها إلى الأصول، باعتبار أن هذه الأصول هي المرجعيات الفكرية التي يستند إليها الفقهاء في اجتهاداتهم وفتاواهم. الثابت المعروف أن علم أصول الفقه كان قد ابتدأ أطواره الأولى على ومن صعيد التدوين والبحث في هذا العصر أيضًا، إذ قام الفقيه المجتهد والأصولي العظيم الإمام محمد بن إدريس الشافعي باستخلاص قواعد هذا العلم وسبكها في بناء منهجي متكامل تمثل في كتابه الشهير «الرسالة». وكما ابتدأ البحث في أصول الفقه مع هذه «الرسالة»، ابتدأ معها أيضا البحث هذا «الجدل الأصولي»، إذ نقف فيها على نماذج كثيرة من هذا الجدل. وعليه، يمكن اعتبار البداية الحقيقية لنشأة البحث في الجدل الأصولي في صورته التطبيقية، هي تلك التي انطلقت مع انطلاقة البحث في أصول الفقه . فهذه إذن مرحلة أولى في نشأة وتطور الجدل الأصولي، أعقبتها مرحلة ثانية شهدت تطورًا متصاعدًا في هذا العلم، وعرف خلالها أزهى أيامه، وهي تلك التي أعقبت مرحلة النشأة والتأسيس، وتنتهي - حسب استقرائي – عند بدايات القرن السابع الهجري، حيث أعقبتها بعد ذلك مرحلة شهد فيها البحث في الجدل الأصولي تراجعا متنازلا حتى ذوى بريقه وتوقف نهائيا، سواء في صورته التطبيقية، أو في صورته النظرية في القرن العاشر الهجري . وعليه يمكن تقسيم هذا الفصل إلى مباحث ثلاثة، كما يلي : المبحث الأول : مرحلة النشأة والتأسيس المبحث الثاني : مرحلة التطور والتكامل المبحث الثالث: مرحلة التراجع والضعف ولا ريب أن وضع الخطوط الفاصلة الدقيقة بين هذه المراحل أمر متعسر جدا
Preface: Chapter Two: The emergence and development of dialectical debate among the usuliyyun. The era of the followers. We concluded in the previous chapter that jurisprudential disagreement had intensified among the Followers and the mujtahid imams, and this disagreement did not stop at the branches (furu'), but extended from them to the principles (usul), considering that these principles are the intellectual references upon which jurists rely in their ijtihad and fatwas. It is an established known fact that the science of usul al-fiqh had begun its first stages from and on the level of codification and research in this era as well, when the great mujtahid jurist and usuli Imam Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i extracted the rules of this science and forged them into an integrated methodological structure represented in his famous book 'al-Risala'. And just as research in usul al-fiqh began with this 'Risala', with it also began research in 'jadal usuli', for we encounter many examples of this jadal therein. Accordingly, the true beginning of research in jadal usuli in its applied form can be considered to be that which started with the launch of research in usul al-fiqh. So this is the first stage in the emergence and development of jadal usuli. It was followed by a second stage that witnessed an escalating development in this science, during which it knew its brightest days. This stage followed the stage of emergence and foundation, and it ends - according to my investigation - at the beginning of the seventh century AH. Then after that came a stage in which research in jadal usuli witnessed a declining regression until its luster faded and it stopped completely, both in its applied form and in its theoretical form, in the tenth century AH. Accordingly, this chapter can be divided into three sections, as follows: Section One: The stage of emergence and foundation. Section Two: The stage of development and integration. Section Three: The stage of decline and weakness. There is no doubt that drawing precise dividing lines between these stages is very difficult.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a preface to a chapter on the emergence and development of jadal usuli (dialectical debate in usul al-fiqh). The author first recaps the intensification of jurisprudential disagreement among the Followers and mujtahid imams, which extended from furu' to usul. He then states that usul al-fiqh as a discipline began its first stages of codification in this era with al-Shafi'i's al-Risala. Importantly, he asserts that jadal usuli research began concurrently with usul al-fiqh research, as the Risala contains many examples of such debate. The author then delineates three historical stages: the first is the stage of emergence and foundation, which began with al-Shafi'i; the second is the stage of development and integration, which lasted until the early 7th century AH; the third is the stage of decline and weakness, which ended in the 10th century AH when the discipline ceased entirely. Finally, he acknowledges the difficulty of precisely demarcating these stages.

The Three Historical Stages of Dialectical Debate Among Usul Scholars
Author outlines the three historical stages of dialectical debate (jadal) among usuliyyin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three historical stages of jadal usuli (dialectical debate in usul al-fiqh) and explain the role of al-Shafi'i in its emergence.

Core Idea
Jadal usuli was born with al-Shafi'i, flourished until the 7th century, then declined into obscurity by the 10th.

This lesson sets the historical stage for understanding how dialectical debate developed within the field of usul al-fiqh. You will learn that jadal usuli did not arise in isolation but emerged alongside the codification of usul al-fiqh itself, beginning with Imam al-Shafi'i's seminal work, al-Risala. The author then proposes a tripartite periodization: emergence, development, and decline, which will serve as a framework for the rest of the chapter.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the link between jurisprudential disagreement and usul
The author recalls that disagreements among jurists extended from subsidiary rulings to fundamental principles, showing the need for systematic usul al-fiqh. This context explains why dialectical debate on principles became necessary.
2
Identify al-Shafi'i and al-Risala as the starting point
Imam al-Shafi'i is credited with extracting and systematizing the rules of usul al-fiqh in al-Risala. The author emphasizes that jadal usuli began simultaneously, as al-Risala contains early examples of such debate.
Thus, the first stage is tied to the founding of usul al-fiqh.
3
Distinguish the three stages
Stage 1: Emergence and establishment (with al-Shafi'i). Stage 2: Development and integration (up to early 7th century AH). Stage 3: Regression and weakness (ending in 10th century AH). The author notes that drawing precise boundaries is difficult but uses prominent usuli figures as markers.
Focus on the key characteristics: growth in stage 2, decline in stage 3.
4
Understand the author's cautious periodization
The author admits that this division is a personal ijtihad and may be imprecise. This humility is important: historical periodizations are tools, not absolute facts.

توطئة : الفصل الثاني نشأة وتطور البحث الجدلي عند الأصوليين انتهينا في الفصل السابق إلى أن الخلاف الفقهي كان قد احتدم في التابعين والأئمة المجتهدين، وهذا الخلاف لم يتوقف عند الفروع، بل تعداه منها إلى الأصول، باعتبار أن هذه الأصول هي المرجعيات الفكرية التي يستند إليها الفقهاء في اجتهاداتهم وفتاواهم. الثابت المعروف أن علم أصول الفقه كان قد ابتدأ أطواره الأولى على ومن صعيد التدوين والبحث في هذا العصر أيضًا، إذ قام الفقيه المجتهد والأصولي العظيم الإمام محمد بن إدريس الشافعي باستخلاص قواعد هذا العلم وسبكها في بناء منهجي متكامل تمثل في كتابه الشهير «الرسالة». وكما ابتدأ البحث في أصول الفقه مع هذه «الرسالة»، ابتدأ معها أيضا البحث «الجدل الأصولي»، إذ نقف فيها على نماذج كثيرة من هذا الجدل. وعليه، يمكن اعتبار البداية الحقيقية لنشأة البحث في الجدل الأصولي في صورته التطبيقية، هي تلك التي انطلقت مع انطلاقة البحث في أصول الفقه . فهذه إذن مرحلة أولى في نشأة وتطور الجدل الأصولي، أعقبتها مرحلة ثانية شهدت تطورًا متصاعدًا في هذا العلم، وعرف خلالها أزهى أيامه، وهي تلك التي أعقبت مرحلة النشأة والتأسيس، وتنتهي - حسب استقرائي – عند بدايات القرن السابع الهجري، حيث أعقبتها بعد ذلك مرحلة شهد فيها البحث في الجدل الأصولي تراجعا متنازلا حتى ذوى بريقه وتوقف نهائيا، سواء في صورته التطبيقية، أو في صورته النظرية في القرن العاشر الهجري . وعليه يمكن تقسيم هذا الفصل إلى مباحث ثلاثة، كما يلي : المبحث الأول : مرحلة النشأة والتأسيس المبحث الثاني : مرحلة التطور والتكامل المبحث الثالث: مرحلة التراجع والضعف ولا ريب أن وضع الخطوط الفاصلة الدقيقة بين هذه المراحل أمر متعسر جدا، ولكنني حاولت قدر الإمكان أن أضع فواصل زمنية ترتبط بشخصيات أصولية بارزة، وعلى كل حال فهو مجرد اجتهاد قد يخطئ وقد يصيب، وأرجو أن يكون مصيبا إن شاء الله تعالى .
Preface: Chapter Two: The emergence and development of dialectical research among the usul scholars. We concluded in the previous chapter that jurisprudential disagreement had intensified among the Followers and the mujtahid imams, and this disagreement did not stop at subsidiary branches, but rather extended from them to the principles, considering that these principles are the intellectual references upon which jurists rely in their ijtihad and fatwas. It is well established that the science of usul al-fiqh had begun its early stages with codification and research in this era as well, as the great jurist and mujtahid, Imam Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i, extracted the rules of this science and forged them into an integrated methodological structure represented in his famous book 'al-Risala.' And just as research in usul al-fiqh began with this 'Risala,' research in 'al-jadal al-usuli' also began with it, as we find in it many examples of this dialectic. Accordingly, the true beginning of the emergence of research in dialectical debate in its applied form can be considered to be that which started with the start of research in usul al-fiqh. So this is the first stage in the emergence and development of usuli dialectic, followed by a second stage that witnessed an escalating development in this science, and during which it knew its finest days, which followed the stage of emergence and establishment, and ends - according to my induction - at the beginnings of the seventh century AH, after which was followed by a stage in which research in usuli dialectic witnessed a declining regression until its brilliance withered and it stopped completely, both in its applied form and in its theoretical form in the tenth century AH. Accordingly, this chapter can be divided into three sections, as follows: The first section: The stage of emergence and establishment. The second section: The stage of development and integration. The third section: The stage of regression and weakness. There is no doubt that drawing precise dividing lines between these stages is very difficult, but I have tried as much as possible to place chronological breaks linked to prominent usuli figures, and in any case it is merely an ijtihad that may err or be correct, and I hope that it is correct, God willing.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a preface to the second chapter, establishing the historical framework for the study of dialectical debate (jadal) among usul scholars. The author begins by recalling the previous chapter's conclusion that jurisprudential disagreements among the Followers and mujtahid imams were not limited to subsidiary branches but extended to fundamental principles (usul). This sets the stage for the importance of usul al-fiqh as the intellectual foundation for ijtihad. The author then notes that usul al-fiqh as a systematic discipline began with Imam al-Shafi'i's 'al-Risala,' where he extracted and structured its rules. Simultaneously, the practice of 'al-jadal al-usuli' (dialectical debate in usul) emerged alongside, as evidenced by examples within al-Risala itself. Thus, the author identifies the first stage as the period of emergence and establishment, coinciding with the birth of usul al-fiqh. The second stage is one of development and integration, reaching its peak and extending until the early 7th century AH. Finally, a third stage of regression and decline follows, where the practice withered and ceased entirely by the 10th century AH, both in applied and theoretical aspects. The author acknowledges the difficulty of precisely demarcating these stages but offers a tentative periodization based on prominent usuli figures. The passage concludes by dividing the chapter into three sections corresponding to these stages, emphasizing that this classification is a personal ijtihad subject to error.

Key Terms
الجدل الأصولي (al-jadal al-usuli): Dialectical debate focused on the principles of jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh), involving structured argumentation between opposing views within the Islamic legal tradition. [Note: This term is used here specifically for debate within usul al-fiqh; in later periods it may be subsumed under broader 'jadal' or 'munazara' literature.]
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The foundational principles and methodology of Islamic jurisprudence, first systematically formulated by al-Shafi'i in al-Risala. [Note: The term remains stable across the tradition, though later scholars expanded its scope.]
الرسالة (al-Risala): Al-Shafi'i's seminal work that established the discipline of usul al-fiqh and included early examples of dialectical debate. [Note: No significant shift; it is consistently regarded as the first systematic work in usul al-fiqh.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) With the Followers' disagreements
B) With Imam al-Shafi'i's al-Risala
C) In the 7th century AH
D) In the 10th century AH

Key Takeaway
The three-stage model of jadal usuli — emergence, development, decline — shows that dialectical debate was integral to usul al-fiqh from its earliest codification by al-Shafi'i.

The Dialectical Method in Hanbali Usul al-Fiqh
Describes the book's significance and dialectical method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the stages of the dialectical method as described in this passage and apply it to reconstruct a Hanbali usul argument.

Core Idea
The dialectical method transforms a usul work from a mere summary into a weapon for madhhab defense.

This passage introduces Ibn al-Farra's 'al-'Uddah fi Usul al-Fiqh', praising its role as a defensive tool for Hanbali jurisprudence. The author describes a structured dialectical method that goes beyond stating rules to actively refuting opponents. Understanding this method is key to appreciating how classical usul works functioned in inter-madhhab debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author's Stated Purpose
Find where the author describes the book's goal. Look for phrases indicating defense of the Hanbali school, such as 'defensive tool'.
The passage states it is a 'comprehensive defensive tool' for the rules of the Hanbali school.
2
List the Steps of the Dialectical Method
The passage outlines: a) establish the Hanbali position, b) mention opponents, c) present evidence from Quran and Sunnah with inference, d) present opponents' evidence and respond/refute.
These steps form the core of the method.
3
Observe the Attention to Terminology
Note that the author also defines usul terms precisely in language and technical usage.
This shows the method includes linguistic and conceptual clarity.
4
Contrast with Non-Dialectical Approaches
Consider what a non-dialectical method would look like (e.g., just stating rules without refutation).
This highlights the defensive, comparative nature of the work.

في أصول الفقه هذا الكتاب الذي يعد بحق «مصدرًا أصيلا من أصول الحنابلة، لما لمؤلفه من الدراية الكافية بالمذهب الحنبلي، أصولا وفروعًا، وهو يمتاز بأن مصادره أصيلة وبخاصة ما ينقله المؤلف عن الإمام أحمد من الروايات، وما ينقله عن أصحابه من الآراء، ولم يقتصر على إيراد رواية واحدة عن الإمام أحمد، بل ساق كثيرًا من الروايات وبخاصة إذا كانت مختلفة. وليست هذه هي الميزة الوحيدة لهذا الكتاب فإن له مزايا أخرى، منها أنه يعتبر أداة دفاعية متكاملة عن قواعد المذهب الحنبلي في أصول الفقه، إذ أداره المؤلف على الطريقة الجدلية الهادفة إلى تقرير أصول المذهب والدفاع عنها في مقابل آراء المذاهب الأخرى. وتقوم طريقة المؤلف في دراسة القواعد الأصولية على تقرير هذه القواعد وفق مذهب الإمام أحمد بن حنبل رحمه الله، ثم ذكر من يخالفونه من العلماء في رأيه، ثم عرض أدلة المذهب في المسألة موضع النزاع بإسهاب من الكتاب والسنة مع بيان أوجه الاستدلال بها، ثم ذكر أدلة المخالفين والإجابة عنها ونقض الاستشهاد بها، كما حرص أيضًا على ضبط المصطلحات الأصولية وتحديد معانيها في اللغة والاصطلاح هذا التحديد الذي يوظفه بعد ذلك في تفصيل القول في المسائل المتشعبة التي يحرص على تحرير محل النزاع فيها وبيانه. في هذه المرحلة يبرز عالم جليل كان له صيته الواسع بين علماء الشافعية في عصره، وهو المعروف في زمانه بابن الفراء، ولد سنة 380هـ/ 990م، في بيت علم، طلب العلم على يد أبيه وعلى يد المحدث علي بن معروف ثم ارتحل إلى مكة ودمشق وحلب، وتولى التدريس في جامع المنصور ببغداد وتولى القضاء سنة 447هـ، وظل فيه إلى أن توفي سنة 458هـ/ 1065م، كان زاهدًا ورعًا متعففًا عن الدنيا وأهلها، ترك تصانيف كثيرة، منها: أحكام القرآن، مسائل الإيمان، المعتمد في أصول الدين، عيون المسائل، العدة في أصول الفقه، الأحكام السلطانية، وغيرها.
In usul al-fiqh, this book is rightly considered an authentic source of Hanbali principles, due to its author's sufficient knowledge of the Hanbali school, both in principles and branches. It is distinguished by its authentic sources, especially the author's transmission of narrations from Imam Ahmad and his companions, and he did not limit himself to one narration but brought many, especially when different. Not only that, but the book has other merits, including that it is a comprehensive defensive tool for the rules of the Hanbali school in usul al-fiqh, as the author organized it on the dialectical method aimed at establishing the school's principles and defending them against the views of other schools. The author's method in studying the principles of usul is to establish these rules according to the school of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, then mention those who oppose him among scholars, then present the evidence of the school on the disputed issue at length from the Book and Sunnah, indicating the aspects of inference, then mention the evidence of the opponents and respond to it and refute the citation. He also paid attention to defining usul terminology and specifying its meanings in language and technical terminology, which he then employs in detailing the discourse on the branched issues, striving to clarify the point of dispute. At this point, there emerges a great scholar who had wide renown among the Shafi'i scholars of his time, known in his era as Ibn al-Farra. He was born in 380/990 in a scholarly household, studied under his father and the hadith scholar Ali ibn Ma'ruf, then traveled to Mecca, Damascus, and Aleppo. He taught at the Al-Mansur Mosque in Baghdad and became a judge in 447, remaining in that position until his death in 458/1065. He was ascetic, pious, and abstinent from the world and its people. He left many works, including: Ahkam al-Qur'an, Masa'il al-Iman, al-Mu'tamad fi Usul al-Din, 'Uyun al-Masa'il, al-'Uddah fi Usul al-Fiqh, al-Ahkam al-Sultaniyya, and others.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to a book on usul al-fiqh, praising its merits and describing the author's methodology. The author emphasizes the book's importance as a primary source for Hanbali usul because it relies on authentic narrations from Imam Ahmad. The key feature highlighted is the dialectical (jadali) method: the author first establishes the Hanbali position, then presents opposing views, provides evidence from the Qur'an and Sunnah, and finally refutes the opponents' evidence. The passage then provides a biography of the author, Ibn al-Farra, noting his scholarly lineage, travels, teaching, and judgeship, as well as his asceticism and list of works. This framework shows that the book is not merely a presentation of rules but a defensive tool crafted to uphold the Hanbali school against other madhahib, using both transmitted and rational arguments.

Key Terms
الطريقة الجدلية
أصول الفقه
المذهب الحنبلي

The dialectical method in usul al-fiqh involves sequentially establishing one's own madhhab position, presenting opposing views, providing textual evidence, and then refuting the opponents' evidence.

Al-Shirazi's Methodological Evolution in Usul al-Fiqh
Describes al-Shirazi's dialectical works and their improvements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the dialectical methods of al-Shirazi's al-Tabsira and Sharh al-Luma', identifying the key improvements in the latter.

Core Idea
Al-Shirazi refined his dialectical method by defining the point of dispute and addressing all opinions.

Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi wrote three influential works in usul al-fiqh, each with a different purpose and method. This lesson examines how his later work, Sharh al-Luma', corrected the shortcomings of the earlier al-Tabsira, providing a model for applied dialectical writing in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three works
Note the titles: al-Luma' (a concise summary), al-Tabsira (an applied dialectical book), and Sharh al-Luma' (a detailed commentary). Understand the purpose of each.
Al-Luma' is a textbook; al-Tabsira is dispute-focused; Sharh al-Luma' is a comprehensive revision.
2
Analyze the criticism of al-Tabsira
The passage highlights two main deficiencies: it does not include all schools or all disputed issues, and it often fails to define the exact point of dispute (tahrir mahall al-niza').
These are methodological weaknesses in dialectical argumentation.
3
Examine the improvements in Sharh al-Luma'
Al-Shirazi remedied these by adopting a simple, detailed style: he presents his view first, then refutes opposing views using both transmitted and rational evidence, covering all well-known opinions.
This makes the work more comprehensive and rigorous.
4
Connect to the broader dialectical tradition
This evolution shows how usul scholars refined the genre of applied dialectic (jadal taṭbīqī) to better defend their school and engage with opponents.
Understanding this helps appreciate later usul works that follow similar methods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو الإمام أبو إسحاق الشيرازي (ت: 476 هـ)، صاحب المؤلفات الكثيرة في مختلف العلوم الشرعية ومنها في أصول الفقه: (اللمع)، و(التبصرة)، و(شرح اللمع). وإذا كان (اللمع) كتابًا مختصرًا ولا يتناول سوى خلاصة قواعد المذهب الشافعي في أصول الفقه فإن كتاب (التبصرة) يعتبر كتابًا جدليًا تطبيقيًا في أصول الفقه، حيث لم يتعرض فيه الشيرازي إلا للمسائل الأصولية المختلف فيها، لكن الذي يشوبه نوعًا ما هو أن المؤلف لم يكن يذكر فيه جميع المذاهب المختلفة في المسألة التي يتعرض لها كما أنه لم يتعرض لجميع المسائل الخلافية في علم الأصول، وإنما تعرض لغالبيتها العظمى، كما يؤخذ عليه عدم تحريره لمحل النزاع في كثير من المسائل المختلف فيها. وقد تدارك الشيرازي هذا النقص في كتابه الآخر (شرح اللمع)، حيث حاول أن يضمنه كل المسائل الأصولية التي تناولها بأسلوب سهل بسيط لا تعقيد فيه ولا التواء، حيث يفصل القول في كل مسألة، ويعرض حولها كل الآراء المشهورة، يبدأ أولا بعرض رأيه هو ثم ينتقل إلى الآراء المخالفة ليدحضها رأيا بعد رأي معتمدا على الحجج النقلية كالقرآن والسنة أو أقوال الصحابة والتابعين، وكذلك على الحجج العقلية، والآراء المخالفة كثيرًا ما تكون للمعتزلة وحتى الأشعرية، وكذلك المالكية والحنفية والظاهرية، والآراء التي يؤيدها عادة هي آراء الشافعية وخاصة آراء أستاذه أبي الطيب الطبري، وإن لاحظ اختلافا داخل مذهبه.
He is Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi (d. 476 AH), author of many works in various Islamic sciences, among them in usul al-fiqh: al-Luma‘, al-Tabsira, and Sharh al-Luma‘. While al-Luma‘ is a concise book covering only the summary of the rules of the Shafi‘i school in usul al-fiqh, the book al-Tabsira is considered an applied dialectical book in usul al-fiqh, in which al-Shirazi only deals with disputed usul issues. However, it is somewhat marred by the fact that the author does not mention all the different schools in the issue he addresses, nor does he cover all the disputed issues in the science of usul; rather, he covers the vast majority. He is also criticized for not clearly defining the point of dispute in many of the contested issues. Al-Shirazi remedied this deficiency in his other book, Sharh al-Luma‘, where he attempted to include all the usul issues he addressed in a simple, straightforward style without complexity or deviation. He goes into detail on each issue and presents all the well-known opinions around it. He begins by presenting his own view, then moves to the opposing views to refute them one by one, relying on transmitted evidence such as the Qur'an, Sunnah, or sayings of the Companions and Successors, as well as rational evidence. The opposing views are often those of the Mu‘tazila, even the Ash‘aris, as well as the Malikis, Hanafis, and Zahiris. The views he typically supports are those of the Shafi‘is, especially the views of his teacher Abu al-Tayyib al-Tabari, although he notes differences within his own school.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage introduces Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi and his works in usul al-fiqh. It contrasts his three books: al-Luma‘ is a concise summary of Shafi‘i usul; al-Tabsira is a dialectical (jadali) work focusing only on disputed issues; and Sharh al-Luma‘ is an improved version that covers all issues comprehensively. The passage notes the shortcomings of al-Tabsira: it does not include all madhahib or all disputed issues, and it often fails to define the point of dispute. Sharh al-Luma‘ corrects this by adopting a clear, detailed method: it presents al-Shirazi's own view, then refutes opposing views using both transmitted and rational evidence. The opponents mentioned include Mu‘tazila, Ash‘aris, Malikis, Hanafis, and Zahiris. The passage illustrates the development of dialectical writing in usul, showing how al-Shirazi systematically refined his approach to better defend the Shafi‘i school.

Key Terms
كتاب جدلي تطبيقي
تحرير محل النزاع
اللمع

Key Takeaway
Al-Shirazi's Sharh al-Luma' represents a methodological advancement in applied dialectical writing by being comprehensive, clear, and rigorous in defining and refuting opposing views.

Lost Works and the Importance of Biographical Dictionaries
Acknowledges existence of other scholars whose works are lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why lost works and biographical dictionaries (kutub al-tarajim) are crucial for understanding the history of jadal in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Lost works remind us that our picture of the past is incomplete.

In this passage, the author acknowledges that his focus on certain scholars does not mean others did not contribute. He points to biographical dictionaries that mention many scholars whose works are now lost or hidden. This lesson examines the significance of such lost works and the role of biographical sources in reconstructing intellectual history.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the author's admission of selectivity
The author says being satisfied with mentioning certain scholars does not mean there were no others. This shows humility and awareness of historical limits.
2
Understand the role of biographical dictionaries (kutub al-tarajim)
These works preserve names and contributions even if the primary works are lost. They are a key source for intellectual history.
3
Reflect on the implications of lost manuscripts
Many works are either lost or still in manuscript libraries. This highlights the fragility of heritage and the ongoing need for manuscript discovery.

هذا وإن اكتفاءنا بذكر جهود هؤلاء العلماء في هذه المرحلة لا يعني أنه لم يكن هناك علماء آخرون قدموا إسهامات في البحث الأصولي على الطريقة الجدلية، فإن كتب التراجم تذكر لنا الكثير من هؤلاء، ولكن مؤلفاتهم لم تصلنا مع الأسف، فهي إما مفقودة تماما أو لا تزال مغمورة في خزائن المخطوطات

The Decline Stage in Usuli Jadal After al-Razi
Author describes the period of decline after al-Razi, listing scholars and their abridged works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the characteristics of the decline stage in usuli jadal and list the main scholars and their abridged works from this period.

Core Idea
After al-Razi, usuli jadal lost its dialectical vigor, becoming a tradition of abridgements.

The passage describes the third stage of usuli jadal following the peak of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. It highlights a shift from independent, critical engagement to mere summarization of earlier masterpieces. Understanding this decline is crucial for recognizing the later development of Islamic legal theory and the preservation of earlier thought through concise textbooks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time frame
The stage begins immediately after Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (d. 606 AH) and extends until the tenth century AH. Note that the author explicitly calls this period a 'stage of decline and weakness'.
The decline is relative to the peak represented by al-Razi's al-Mahsul.
2
Contrast with the previous stage
Earlier works like al-Mahsul actively defended positions and discussed opposing schools. In this stage, works tended to merely state usuli rules without defense or discussion of opposing views. The passage characterizes them as 'merely abridgements and summaries'.
3
List the works and authors
Extract the names and books: al-Mawsili (Mukhtasar al-Mahsul), al-Abyari (Sharh al-Burhan), Ibn Qudamah (Rawdat al-Nazir, abridging al-Mustasfa), al-Tabrizi (Mukhtasar al-Mahsul), and al-Amidi (al-Ihkam, noted as somewhat different).
Al-Amidi's work is highlighted as an exception that still follows the earlier method.
4
Analyze the nature of abridgements
The author criticizes that these works are 'no more than abridgements and summaries', implying a lack of original contribution. However, note that this process preserved and transmitted earlier knowledge. Consider whether abridgement necessarily implies decline or can be a valuable pedagogical tool.
The shift from independent authorship to commentary/abridgement is a key indicator of decline according to the author.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثالث
مرحلة التراجع والضعف
وتبدأ هذه المرحلة مباشرة بعد الإمام فخر الدين الرازي، وتمتد حتى القرن العاشر الهجري .
هذه المرحلة هي الأخرى عرفت التأليف في الجدل الأصولي بجانبيه النظري والتطبيقي، لذلك سنسير فيها وفق ما سرنا عليه في المرحلة التي سبقتها، فندرس أولا ما يتعلق بالجانب التطبيقي، ثم نتبعه بمساهمات أصوليي هذه المرحلة في الجانب النظري .
المطلب الأول : في الجانب التطبيقي
بعد الأوج الذي ارتفع إليه الإمام فخر الدين الرازي في ميدان البحث الأصولي على الطريقة الجدلية تأتي المؤلفات الأصولية التي تلت كتاب «المحصول» لتنزل بالبحث الأصولي على الطريقة الجدلية إلى مستوى أدنى من ذلك بكثير، إذ تراجعت فيها قوة المنهج الجدلي، وبدأ البحث الأصولي يميل نحو الاكتفاء بتقرير القواعد الأصولية دون اللجوء إلى الدفاع عنها أو مناقشة المذاهب المخالفة شأنها، بل إن كتب هذه المرحلة تعتبر في مجملها مختصرات وتلخيصات لكتب المرحلة السابقة لا غير . وهكذا فبعد الارتفاع الذي وصل إليه الرازي، أصبح البحث الجدلي المستقل في أصول الفقه، يتراجع شيئًا فشيئًا، إذ انتقل العلماء من التأليف المستقل، إلى التأليف الذي هو عبارة عن اختصار لكتاب سابق، أو شرح لكتاب موجز أو مطول من كتب السابقين من علماء المرحلة السابقة . فهذا الإمام عماد الدين الموصلي (ت: 608 هـ) يؤلف كتابا يختصر به كتاب الرازي (المحصول)، ويسميه (مختصر المحصول في أصول الفقه)، كما ألف الإمام أبو الحسن الأبياري (ت: 618هـ) كتابا سماه (شرح البرهان لإمام الحرمين) . وألف الإمام ابن قدامة المقدسي (ت : 620 هـ) كتاب (روضة الناظر والمناظر في أصول الفقه، وهو مختصر من كتاب (المستصفى) للغزالي . كما ألف الإمام المظفر التبريزي (ت: 621 هـ) كتاب (مختصر المحصول في الأصول للرازي). ولعل من أبرز الكتب المؤلفة في هذه المرحلة، وأشهرها، كتاب الإحكام في أصول الأحكام للإمام سيف الدين الآمدي . أن الآمدي قد جرى في كتابه على نفس الطريقة التي جرى عليها سابقوه، من حيث يبدأ بتصوير المسألة وذكر الآراء فيها، ثم يبين رأيه المختار،
The Third Section
Stage of Decline and Weakness
This stage begins immediately after Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi and extends until the tenth century AH. This stage also witnessed authorship in usuli dialectic in both its theoretical and applied aspects. Therefore, we will proceed in it as we did in the preceding stage: we first study what relates to the applied aspect, then we follow it with the contributions of the usulis of this stage in the theoretical aspect. The First Subsection: On the Applied Aspect. After the peak that Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi reached in the field of usuli research on the dialectical method, the usuli works that followed the book 'al-Mahsul' brought down usuli research on the dialectical method to a much lower level, as the strength of the dialectical method declined, and usuli research began to incline toward merely stating the usuli rules without resorting to defending them or discussing opposing schools of thought. Rather, the books of this stage are, in their entirety, only abridgements and summaries of the books of the previous stage. Thus, after the peak reached by al-Razi, independent dialectical research in usul al-fiqh gradually declined, as scholars moved from independent authorship to authorship that is an abridgement of a previous book or a commentary on a concise or lengthy book of the earlier scholars from the previous stage. So Imam 'Imad al-Din al-Mawsili (d. 608 AH) authored a book in which he abridges the book of al-Razi ('al-Mahsul') and calls it 'Mukhtasar al-Mahsul fi Usul al-Fiqh'. Likewise, Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Abyari (d. 618 AH) authored a book called 'Sharh al-Burhan li-imam al-Haramayn'. And Imam Ibn Qudamah al-Maqdisi (d. 620 AH) authored the book 'Rawdat al-Nazir wa al-Munazir fi Usul al-Fiqh', which is an abridgement of the book 'al-Mustasfa' by al-Ghazali. Also, Imam al-Muzaffar al-Tabrizi (d. 621 AH) authored the book 'Mukhtasar al-Mahsul fi al-Usul li al-Razi'. Perhaps among the most prominent and famous books authored in this stage is the book 'al-Ihkam fi Usul al-Ahkam' by Imam Sayf al-Din al-Amidi. Al-Amidi followed in his book the same method as his predecessors, in that he begins by depicting the issue and stating the opinions concerning it, then he clarifies his chosen opinion.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a historical survey of the third stage (مرحلة التراجع والضعف) in the development of jadal (dialectical methodology) within usul al-fiqh, following the peak represented by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. The author states that this stage begins right after al-Razi and extends to the 10th century AH. He notes that both theoretical and applied aspects of jadal were still written, but his focus here is on the applied aspect first. He describes a decline: after al-Razi's 'al-Mahsul', later works lost the dialectical vigor and became mere abridgements and summaries of earlier works, avoiding defense or discussion of opposing views. He lists specific scholars and their works as examples: 'Imad al-Din al-Mawsili's abridgement of al-Mahsul; Abu al-Hasan al-Abyari's commentary on al-Juwayni's al-Burhan; Ibn Qudamah's abridgement of al-Ghazali's al-Mustasfa; and al-Muzaffar al-Tabrizi's abridgement of al-Razi's al-Mahsul. The author then highlights al-Amidi's 'al-Ihkam' as a prominent exception, noting that al-Amidi followed his predecessors' method of presenting issues and opinions before stating his preferred view, implying some continuity with earlier methodologies despite the overall decline.

المختصرات والتلخيصات
المحصول
روضة الناظر والمناظر
الإحكام في أصول الأحكام

Key Takeaway

Key Scholars and Works in Jadal
Author enumerates key scholars and their works on jadal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify at least six major scholars and their key works on jadal from the 6th to 9th centuries AH.

Core Idea
Jadal was a distinct Islamic science with a rich tradition of specialized texts.

This passage introduces us to the intellectual landscape of jadal (dialectical disputation) by listing prominent scholars and their contributions. As we study these names and titles, we begin to see how jadal evolved as a disciplined method of argumentation in usul al-fiqh and kalam. This lesson will help you recognize the key figures who shaped this tradition and understand the scope of their works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scholar and work
Start with Abu al-Baqa al-Ukbari (d. 616 AH) and his book 'Al-Munaqqah min al-Khatal fi Ilm al-Jadal'. Note the death date and the title's focus on clarifying confusion in jadal.
2
List the two works of al-Amidi
Sayf al-Din al-Amidi (d. 631 AH) authored 'Ghayat al-Amal fi Ilm al-Jadal' and a commentary on al-Maraghī's work. Recognise the pattern of scholars writing both original texts and commentaries.
3
Explore the diversity of authors
Continue through the list: al-La’ārdī, al-Maraghī, al-Mada’īnī, al-Urmawi, al-Nasafi, al-‘Ijli, Ibn al-Mi’mar, al-Abhari, al-Jazari, and Ibn Taymiyya. Notice the range of death dates and the geographic spread (e.g., Khurasani, Iraqi).
4
Note the inclusion of Ibn Taymiyya
Ibn Taymiyya (d. 827 AH) is listed with his work 'Tanbih al-Rajul'. This shows that even a critic of Aristotelian logic contributed to jadal literature, implying jadal was a distinct discipline.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical listing of key scholars and their works on the science of jadal (dialectical disputation). The author enumerates works from the 6th to the 9th centuries AH, covering a wide range of contributors from different regions and schools. The passage demonstrates the depth and continuity of the jadal tradition, particularly in usul al-fiqh, showing how later scholars built upon earlier foundations. The inclusion of Ibn Taymiyya, known for his critical stance on logic, indicates that jadal was a distinct discipline from Aristotelian logic.
